</tr><tr><td class="hlist" style="padding:0.3em 0.4em 0.3em;font-weight:bold;border-top: 1px solid #aaa; border-bottom: 1px solid #aaa;padding-top:0.15em;">
<a href="/wiki/File:Symbol-hammer-and-sickle.svg" class="image"><img alt="Symbol-hammer-and-sickle.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Symbol-hammer-and-sickle.svg/16px-Symbol-hammer-and-sickle.svg.png" decoding="async" width="16" height="16" class="noviewer" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Symbol-hammer-and-sickle.svg/24px-Symbol-hammer-and-sickle.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Symbol-hammer-and-sickle.svg/32px-Symbol-hammer-and-sickle.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="48" data-file-height="48" /></a> <a href="/wiki/Portal:Communism" title="Portal:Communism">Communism&#32;portal</a></td></tr><tr><td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%;padding-top: 0.6em;"><div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Communism" title="Template:Communism"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Communism" title="Template talk:Communism"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Communism&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Political_science" title="Political science">political science</a>, <b>Marxism–Leninism</b> was the official state ideology of the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> (USSR), of the parties of the <a href="/wiki/Communist_International" title="Communist International">Communist International</a> after <a href="/wiki/Bolshevisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Bolshevisation">Bolshevisation</a>, and is the ideology of <a href="/wiki/Stalinism" title="Stalinism">Stalinist</a> and <a href="/wiki/Maoism" title="Maoism">Maoist</a> political parties.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> The purpose of Marxism–Leninism is the revolutionary transformation of a capitalist state into a socialist state, by way of <a href="/wiki/Two-stage_theory" title="Two-stage theory">two-stage revolution</a>, which is led by a <a href="/wiki/Vanguardism" title="Vanguardism">vanguard party</a> of professional revolutionaries, drawn from the <a href="/wiki/Proletariat" title="Proletariat">proletariat</a>. To realise the two-stage transformation of the state, the vanguard party establishes the <a href="/wiki/Dictatorship_of_the_proletariat" title="Dictatorship of the proletariat">dictatorship of the proletariat</a>, which determines policy through <a href="/wiki/Democratic_centralism" title="Democratic centralism">democratic centralism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Marxist–Leninist <a href="/wiki/Communist_party" title="Communist party">communist party</a> is the vanguard for the organisation of a capitalist society into a socialist society, which is the lower stage of socio-economic development, and progress towards the upper-stage <a href="/wiki/Communist_society" title="Communist society">communist society</a>, which is <a href="/wiki/Stateless_society" title="Stateless society">stateless</a> and <a href="/wiki/Classless_society" title="Classless society">classless</a>; yet features organised public-ownership of the <a href="/wiki/Means_of_production" title="Means of production">means of production</a>, accelerated <a href="/wiki/Industrialisation" title="Industrialisation">industrialisation</a>, pro-active development of the <a href="/wiki/Productive_forces" title="Productive forces">productive forces</a> of society,<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Nationalization" title="Nationalization">nationalised</a> natural resources.<sup id="cite_ref-sioc33_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sioc33-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the late 1920s, after the death of Lenin, Stalin established universal ideologic orthodoxy among the Communist Party, the USSR, and the Communist International, with his coinage <i>Marxism–Leninism</i>, a term which redefined theories of Lenin and <a href="/wiki/Karl_Marx" title="Karl Marx">Karl Marx</a> to establish universal Marxist–Leninist praxis for the exclusive, geopolitical benefit of the USSR.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-made_by_stalin22_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-made_by_stalin22-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> In the late 1930s, Stalin's official textbook <i><a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Communist_Party_of_the_Soviet_Union_(Bolsheviks)" title="History of the Communist Party of the Soviet Union (Bolsheviks)">The History of the Communist Party of the Soviet Union (Bolsheviks)</a></i> (1938), made the term <i>Marxism–Leninism</i> common political-science usage among communists and non-communists.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Critical of Stalin's <a href="/wiki/Political_economy" title="Political economy">political economy</a> and <a href="/wiki/One-party_state" title="One-party state">single-party</a> government in the USSR, the Italian <a href="/wiki/Left_communism" title="Left communism">Left-communist</a> <a href="/wiki/Amadeo_Bordiga" title="Amadeo Bordiga">Amadeo Bordiga</a> said that Marxism–Leninism was a form of political opportunism, which preserved rather than destroyed capitalism, because of the claim that the exchange of commodities would occur under socialism; and the use of <a href="/wiki/Popular_front" title="Popular front">popular front</a> organisations by the Communist International;<sup id="cite_ref-dialougestalin_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dialougestalin-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> and that a political vanguard organised by <a href="/wiki/Organic_centralism" title="Organic centralism">organic centralism</a> was more effective than a vanguard organised by democratic centralism.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> The American Marxist <a href="/wiki/Raya_Dunayevskaya" title="Raya Dunayevskaya">Raya Dunayevskaya</a> dismissed Marxism–Leninism as a type of <a href="/wiki/State_capitalism" title="State capitalism">state capitalism</a><sup id="cite_ref-statecap3_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-statecap3-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> because: (i) <a href="/wiki/State_ownership" title="State ownership">state ownership</a> of the means of production is a form of state capitalism;<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> (ii) the dictatorship of the proletariat is a form of democracy, and single-party rule is undemocratic,<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> and (iii) Marxism–Leninism is neither <a href="/wiki/Marxism" title="Marxism">Marxism</a> nor <a href="/wiki/Leninism" title="Leninism">Leninism</a>, but a composite ideology that Stalin used to expediently determine what is communism and what is not communism among the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Bloc" title="Eastern Bloc">Eastern Bloc</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-sioc32_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sioc32-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marxism%E2%80%93Leninism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/State_ideology_of_the_Soviet_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="State ideology of the Soviet Union">State ideology of the Soviet Union</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Leninism">Leninism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marxism%E2%80%93Leninism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Leninism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Stalin-Lenin-Kalinin-1919.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Stalin-Lenin-Kalinin-1919.jpg/350px-Stalin-Lenin-Kalinin-1919.jpg" decoding="async" width="350" height="181" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Stalin-Lenin-Kalinin-1919.jpg/525px-Stalin-Lenin-Kalinin-1919.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Stalin-Lenin-Kalinin-1919.jpg/700px-Stalin-Lenin-Kalinin-1919.jpg 2x" data-file-width="880" data-file-height="456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Stalin-Lenin-Kalinin-1919.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Old_Bolsheviks" class="mw-redirect" title="Old Bolsheviks">Old Bolsheviks</a> Stalin, Lenin and <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Kalinin" title="Mikhail Kalinin">Mikhail Kalinin</a> in 1919</div></div></div>
<p>In 1929, within five years of the <a href="/wiki/Death_of_Vladimir_Lenin" class="mw-redirect" title="Death of Vladimir Lenin">death of Vladimir Lenin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stalin" class="mw-redirect" title="Stalin">Stalin</a> was the <a href="/wiki/List_of_leaders_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="List of leaders of the Soviet Union">ruler of the Soviet Union</a> who flouted, abided, and applied the socialist principles of Lenin and Marx as political expediencies used to realise his plans for the USSR and for <a href="/wiki/World_socialism" class="mw-redirect" title="World socialism">world socialism</a>; most of which contradicted Lenin's plans for establishing socialism.<sup id="cite_ref-stalin_follow_marx_lenin_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stalin_follow_marx_lenin-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Stalin justified his régime's deviations from Lenin's practices with the book <i>Concerning Questions of Leninism</i> (1926), in which Stalin represented Marxism–Leninism as a separate communist ideology, which featured an <a href="/wiki/Totalitarianism" title="Totalitarianism">omniscient leader</a>, hierarchies of one global communist party and communist vanguard parties in each country of the world.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-made_by_stalin22_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-made_by_stalin22-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> Stalin's interpretations of Lenin and Marx became <a href="/wiki/Stalinism" title="Stalinism">Stalinism</a>, the official <a href="/wiki/State_ideology_of_the_Soviet_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="State ideology of the Soviet Union">state ideology of the Soviet Union</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Stalinism">Stalinism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marxism%E2%80%93Leninism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Stalinism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>As the <a href="/wiki/Left_Opposition" title="Left Opposition">Left Opposition</a> to Stalin within the Communist Party and the Soviet government, <a href="/wiki/Leon_Trotsky" title="Leon Trotsky">Leon Trotsky</a> and the Trotskyists argued that Stalin's Marxist–Leninist ideology contradicted <a href="/wiki/Marxism" title="Marxism">Marxism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Leninism" title="Leninism">Leninism</a> in theory and in practice, and thus was illegitimate socialist philosophy for the practical implementation of Socialism in Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Moreover, within the Party, the Trotskyists identified their communist ideology as Bolshevik–Leninism (<a href="/wiki/Trotskyism" title="Trotskyism">Trotskyism</a>), to politically differentiate their ideology from the ideology Stalin used to justify and implement his theory of <a href="/wiki/Socialism_in_One_Country" title="Socialism in One Country">Socialism in One Country</a> (1924).
</p><p>In Marxist political discourse the term <i>Marxism–Leninism</i>, denoting and connoting the theory and praxis of <i>Stalinism</i>, has two usages: (i) praise of Joseph Stalin, by Stalinists who believe Stalin successfully developed Lenin's legacy; and (ii) criticism of Stalin, by Stalinists who repudiate Stalin's political purges, social-class repressions, and bureaucratic terrorism.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Maoism">Maoism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marxism%E2%80%93Leninism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Maoism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Consequent to the <a href="/wiki/Sino-Soviet_split" title="Sino-Soviet split">Sino-Soviet split</a> (1956–1966), in each socialist country, the Communist Party of China (CPC) and the Communist Party of the Soviet Union (CPSU) each claimed to be the sole heir-and-successor to Stalin, regarding the correct interpretation of Marxism–Leninism, and thus ideological leader of <a href="/wiki/World_communism" title="World communism">world communism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-World_History_2000._p._769_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_History_2000._p._769-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> In that vein, the <i><a href="/wiki/History_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="History of the People&#39;s Republic of China">History of the People's Republic of China</a></i> represents <a href="/wiki/Maoism" title="Maoism">Maoism</a> (urban Marxism–Leninism adapted to pre-industrial China) as Mao Zedong's fundamental up-dating and adaptation of <a href="/wiki/Leninism" title="Leninism">Leninism</a> to Chinese conditions, in which revolutionary praxis is primary and ideologic orthodoxy is secondary;<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> and the <i>Thought of Mao Zedong</i> became the official state ideology of the PRC.<sup id="cite_ref-Modern_Thought_1999_p._501_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Modern_Thought_1999_p._501-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Sino-Albanian_split" title="Sino-Albanian split">Sino-Albanian split</a> (1972–1978) was caused by <a href="/wiki/Socialist_People%27s_Republic_of_Albania" class="mw-redirect" title="Socialist People&#39;s Republic of Albania">Socialist Albania</a>'s rejection of the PRC's <i><a href="/wiki/Realpolitik" title="Realpolitik">Realpolitik</a></i> of Sino–American rapprochement, specifically the <a href="/wiki/1972_Nixon_visit_to_China" class="mw-redirect" title="1972 Nixon visit to China">Mao–Nixon meeting</a>&#160; (1972), which the <a href="/wiki/Anti-revisionist" class="mw-redirect" title="Anti-revisionist">anti-revisionist</a> <a href="/wiki/Albanian_Labor_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="Albanian Labor Party">Albanian Labor Party</a> perceived as an ideological betrayal of Mao's own <a href="/wiki/Three_Worlds_Theory" title="Three Worlds Theory">Three Worlds Theory</a>, which excluded such political relations of rapprochement. To the Albanians, the Chinese dealings with the U.S. were a lessening of Mao's ideologic and practical commitments to <a href="/wiki/Proletarian_internationalism" title="Proletarian internationalism">proletarian internationalism</a>. <a href="/wiki/Enver_Hoxha" title="Enver Hoxha">Enver Hoxha</a>, the head of the Albanian Labor Party, theorised an anti-revisionist Marxism–Leninism referred to as <a href="/wiki/Hoxhaism" title="Hoxhaism">Hoxhaism</a>, which attempted&#160; to retain an 'authentic' socialism in comparison to the post-Stalinist Soviet Union.
</p><p>As revolutionary praxis, Maoism is the ideology of communist parties philosophically akin to the Communist Party of China. Since the death of Mao Zedong, in 1976, the <a href="/wiki/Shining_Path" title="Shining Path">Shining Path</a> (<i>Sendero Luminoso</i>) Communist Party of Peru coined the term <i><a href="/wiki/Marxism%E2%80%93Leninism%E2%80%93Maoism" title="Marxism–Leninism–Maoism">Marxism–Leninism–Maoism</a></i> to identify the contemporary Marxism that is readily adaptable to local conditions in the countries of <a href="/wiki/Three-world_model" title="Three-world model">Third-world</a> South America.<sup id="cite_ref-Modern_Thought_1999_p._501_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Modern_Thought_1999_p._501-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span id="Marxist.E2.80.93Leninist_state"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Marxist–Leninist_state">Marxist–Leninist state</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marxism%E2%80%93Leninism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Marxist–Leninist state">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In the one-party Marxist–Leninist state, the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="Communist Party">Communist Party</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Vanguardism" title="Vanguardism">political vanguard</a> who guides the working class and the proletariat in establishing the foundations (social, economic, cultural) of a <a href="/wiki/Socialism" title="Socialism">socialist society</a>, which is realised with <a href="/wiki/Two-stage_theory" title="Two-stage theory">two-stage</a> revolutionary development: (i) from a capitalist state to a <a href="/wiki/Socialist_state" title="Socialist state">socialist state</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Alexander_Shtromas_2003._p._18_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Alexander_Shtromas_2003._p._18-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> and (ii) from a socialist society to a <a href="/wiki/Communist_society" title="Communist society">communist society</a>, which has no <a href="/wiki/Social_stratification" title="Social stratification">social stratification</a> and no <a href="/wiki/Sexism" title="Sexism">institutional sexism</a>, where <a href="/wiki/From_each_according_to_his_ability,_to_each_according_to_his_need" class="mw-redirect" title="From each according to his ability, to each according to his need">men and women work and consume according to their abilities and needs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> The socialist society is instituted and governed through the <a href="/wiki/Dictatorship_of_the_proletariat" title="Dictatorship of the proletariat">dictatorship of the proletariat</a> to define and decide, implement and realise policy through <a href="/wiki/Democratic_centralism" title="Democratic centralism">democratic centralism</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-Albert_pp._24–25_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Albert_pp._24–25-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> and government offices are peopled by election at the local, regional, and national levels, usually direct election; however, indirect election also features in the Marxist–Leninist practices of the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="People&#39;s Republic of China">People's Republic of China</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Cuba" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of Cuba">Republic of Cuba</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Yugoslavia" class="mw-redirect" title="Socialist Yugoslavia">Socialist Yugoslavia</a> (1943–1992).<sup id="cite_ref-Pons_p._306_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pons_p._306-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marxism%E2%80%93Leninism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The goal of Marxist–Leninist <a href="/wiki/Political_economy" title="Political economy">political economy</a> is the emancipation of men and women from the <a href="/wiki/Dehumanisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Dehumanisation">dehumanisation</a> caused by mechanistic work that is <a href="/wiki/Theory_of_alienation" class="mw-redirect" title="Theory of alienation">psychologically alienating</a> (without work–life balance), which is performed in exchange for <a href="/wiki/Wage" title="Wage">wages</a> that give limited financial-access to the material necessities of life (i.e. food and shelter). That personal and societal emancipation from <a href="/wiki/Poverty" title="Poverty">poverty</a> (material necessity) would maximise individual liberty, by enabling men and women to pursue their interests and innate talents (artistic, intellectual, industrial, etc.) whilst working by choice, without the economic coercion of poverty. In the <a href="/wiki/Communist_society" title="Communist society">communist society</a> of upper-stage economic development, the elimination of alienating labour (mechanistic work) depends upon the developments of <a href="/wiki/High_technology" class="mw-redirect" title="High technology">high technology</a> that improve the means of production and the means of distribution.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%E2%80%9CStrengthen_working_discipline_in_collective_farms%E2%80%9D_%E2%80%93_Uzbek,_Tashkent,_1933_(Mardjani).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/%E2%80%9CStrengthen_working_discipline_in_collective_farms%E2%80%9D_%E2%80%93_Uzbek%2C_Tashkent%2C_1933_%28Mardjani%29.jpg/350px-%E2%80%9CStrengthen_working_discipline_in_collective_farms%E2%80%9D_%E2%80%93_Uzbek%2C_Tashkent%2C_1933_%28Mardjani%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="350" height="234" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/%E2%80%9CStrengthen_working_discipline_in_collective_farms%E2%80%9D_%E2%80%93_Uzbek%2C_Tashkent%2C_1933_%28Mardjani%29.jpg/525px-%E2%80%9CStrengthen_working_discipline_in_collective_farms%E2%80%9D_%E2%80%93_Uzbek%2C_Tashkent%2C_1933_%28Mardjani%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/%E2%80%9CStrengthen_working_discipline_in_collective_farms%E2%80%9D_%E2%80%93_Uzbek%2C_Tashkent%2C_1933_%28Mardjani%29.jpg/700px-%E2%80%9CStrengthen_working_discipline_in_collective_farms%E2%80%9D_%E2%80%93_Uzbek%2C_Tashkent%2C_1933_%28Mardjani%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="893" data-file-height="598" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%E2%80%9CStrengthen_working_discipline_in_collective_farms%E2%80%9D_%E2%80%93_Uzbek,_Tashkent,_1933_(Mardjani).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>In 1933, <a href="/wiki/Soviet_propaganda" class="mw-redirect" title="Soviet propaganda">Soviet propaganda</a> encouraged peasants and farmers to strengthen working discipline in <a href="/wiki/Collectivization_in_the_Soviet_Union" title="Collectivization in the Soviet Union">collective farms</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Azeri_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="Azeri Soviet Socialist Republic">Azeri Soviet Socialist Republic</a> (Azerbaijan)</div></div></div>
<p>To meet the material needs of a socialist society, the Marxist–Leninist state uses a <a href="/wiki/Planned_economy" title="Planned economy">planned economy</a> to co-ordinate the <a href="/wiki/Means_of_production" title="Means of production">means of production</a> and of distribution to supply and deliver the goods and services required throughout society and the national economy.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Wages" class="mw-redirect" title="Wages">wages</a> of the worker are determined according to the type of skills and the type of work he or she can perform within the national economy.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> Moreover, the economic value of the goods and services produced is based upon their <a href="/wiki/Use_value" title="Use value">use value</a> (as material objects) and not upon the <a href="/wiki/Labor_theory_of_value" title="Labor theory of value">cost of production</a> ("value") or the <a href="/wiki/Marginal_Utility" class="mw-redirect" title="Marginal Utility">exchange value</a> (marginal utility).<sup id="cite_ref-Pons_p._139_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pons_p._139-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the 1920s, the Bolshevik government's economic development realised the <a href="/wiki/Industrialization_in_the_USSR#Industrialization_in_practice" class="mw-redirect" title="Industrialization in the USSR">rapid industrialisation</a> of the Soviet Union with pragmatic programs of <a href="/wiki/Social_engineering_(political_science)" title="Social engineering (political science)">social engineering</a> that transplanted peasant populations to the cities, where they were educated and trained as <a href="/wiki/Industrial_workers" class="mw-redirect" title="Industrial workers">industrial workers</a>, and then became the workforce of the new factories and industries. Likewise, the farmer populations worked the <a href="/wiki/Collectivisation_in_the_Soviet_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Collectivisation in the Soviet Union">system of collective farms</a> to grow food to feed the industrial workers in the industrialised cities. Hence, in the 1930s, the Marxist–Leninist society of Russia featured austere social-equality, based upon <a href="/wiki/Asceticism" title="Asceticism">asceticism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Egalitarianism" title="Egalitarianism">egalitarianism</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Self-sacrifice" class="mw-redirect" title="Self-sacrifice">self-sacrifice</a> — yet the Bolshevik Party recognised human nature, and semi-officially allowed some limited, small-scale capitalism to stimulate the <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Economy of the Soviet Union">economy of the Soviet Union</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Orthodox_Marxism" title="Orthodox Marxism">Orthodox Marxism</a>, the socialist society originally was equivalent to the communist society; yet, in the economic praxis of Bolshevik Russia, in defining the differences of political economy, between <a href="/wiki/Socialism" title="Socialism">Socialism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Communism" title="Communism">Communism</a>, Lenin explained their conceptual similarity to Marx's descriptions of the lower-stage and the upper-stage of economic development. That immediately after a proletarian revolution, in the socialist lower-stage society, the practical economy must be based upon the individual labour contributed by men and women;<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> that paid labour would be the basis of the communist upper-stage society that has realised the social precept of the slogan: <i><a href="/wiki/From_each_according_to_his_ability,_to_each_according_to_his_need" class="mw-redirect" title="From each according to his ability, to each according to his need">From Each According to His Ability, to Each According to His Need</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Society">Society</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marxism%E2%80%93Leninism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Society">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%D0%A7%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%B1%D1%8B_%D0%B1%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%8C%D1%88%D0%B5_%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%B5%D1%82%D1%8C_%E2%80%94_%D0%BD%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%BE_%D0%B1%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%8C%D1%88%D0%B5_%D0%BF%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B8%D0%B7%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B4%D0%B8%D1%82%D1%8C._%D0%A7%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%B1%D1%8B_%D0%B1%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%8C%D1%88%D0%B5_%D0%BF%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B8%D0%B7%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B4%D0%B8%D1%82%D1%8C_%E2%80%94_%D0%BD%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%BE_%D0%B1%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%8C%D1%88%D0%B5_%D0%B7%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%82%D1%8C.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/%D0%A7%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%B1%D1%8B_%D0%B1%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%8C%D1%88%D0%B5_%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%B5%D1%82%D1%8C_%E2%80%94_%D0%BD%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%BE_%D0%B1%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%8C%D1%88%D0%B5_%D0%BF%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B8%D0%B7%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B4%D0%B8%D1%82%D1%8C._%D0%A7%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%B1%D1%8B_%D0%B1%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%8C%D1%88%D0%B5_%D0%BF%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B8%D0%B7%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B4%D0%B8%D1%82%D1%8C_%E2%80%94_%D0%BD%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%BE_%D0%B1%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%8C%D1%88%D0%B5_%D0%B7%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%82%D1%8C.jpg/300px-thumbnail.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="416" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/%D0%A7%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%B1%D1%8B_%D0%B1%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%8C%D1%88%D0%B5_%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%B5%D1%82%D1%8C_%E2%80%94_%D0%BD%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%BE_%D0%B1%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%8C%D1%88%D0%B5_%D0%BF%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B8%D0%B7%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B4%D0%B8%D1%82%D1%8C._%D0%A7%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%B1%D1%8B_%D0%B1%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%8C%D1%88%D0%B5_%D0%BF%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B8%D0%B7%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B4%D0%B8%D1%82%D1%8C_%E2%80%94_%D0%BD%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%BE_%D0%B1%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%8C%D1%88%D0%B5_%D0%B7%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%82%D1%8C.jpg/450px-thumbnail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/%D0%A7%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%B1%D1%8B_%D0%B1%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%8C%D1%88%D0%B5_%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%B5%D1%82%D1%8C_%E2%80%94_%D0%BD%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%BE_%D0%B1%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%8C%D1%88%D0%B5_%D0%BF%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B8%D0%B7%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B4%D0%B8%D1%82%D1%8C._%D0%A7%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%B1%D1%8B_%D0%B1%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%8C%D1%88%D0%B5_%D0%BF%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B8%D0%B7%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B4%D0%B8%D1%82%D1%8C_%E2%80%94_%D0%BD%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%BE_%D0%B1%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%8C%D1%88%D0%B5_%D0%B7%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%82%D1%8C.jpg/600px-thumbnail.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2738" data-file-height="3793" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%D0%A7%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%B1%D1%8B_%D0%B1%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%8C%D1%88%D0%B5_%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%B5%D1%82%D1%8C_%E2%80%94_%D0%BD%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%BE_%D0%B1%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%8C%D1%88%D0%B5_%D0%BF%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B8%D0%B7%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B4%D0%B8%D1%82%D1%8C._%D0%A7%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%B1%D1%8B_%D0%B1%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%8C%D1%88%D0%B5_%D0%BF%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B8%D0%B7%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B4%D0%B8%D1%82%D1%8C_%E2%80%94_%D0%BD%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%BE_%D0%B1%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%8C%D1%88%D0%B5_%D0%B7%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%82%D1%8C.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A 1920 <a href="/wiki/Agitprop" title="Agitprop">Bolshevik pro-education propaganda</a> which reads the following: "In order to have more, it is necessary to produce more. In order to produce more, it is necessary to know more."</div></div></div>
<p>To develop a communist society, the Marxist–Leninist state provides for the national welfare with <a href="/wiki/Universal_healthcare" class="mw-redirect" title="Universal healthcare">universal healthcare</a>, free <a href="/wiki/Public_education" class="mw-redirect" title="Public education">public education</a> (academic, technical, professional), and the <a href="/wiki/Welfare_state" title="Welfare state">social benefits</a> (childcare, continuing education, etc.) necessary to increase the productivity of the workers, and thus the socialist economy.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> As part of the planned economy, the welfare state is meant to develop the <a href="/wiki/Proletariat" title="Proletariat">proletariat</a>'s education (academic and technical) and their <a href="/wiki/Class_consciousness" title="Class consciousness">class consciousness</a> (political education) to facilitate their contextual understanding of the historical development of communism, as presented in <a href="/wiki/Marx%27s_theory_of_history" class="mw-redirect" title="Marx&#39;s theory of history">Marx's theory of history</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The judicial reformation of <a href="/wiki/Family_law" title="Family law">family law</a> eliminates <a href="/wiki/Patriarchy" title="Patriarchy">patriarchy</a> from the legal system, which facilitates the political <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_liberation" class="mw-redirect" title="Women&#39;s liberation">emancipation of women</a> from <a href="/wiki/Traditionalist_conservatism" title="Traditionalist conservatism">traditional</a> social inferiority and <a href="/wiki/Exploitation_of_labour" title="Exploitation of labour">economic exploitation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> The reformation of <a href="/wiki/Civil_law_(legal_system)" title="Civil law (legal system)">civil law</a> made <a href="/wiki/Marriage" title="Marriage">marriage</a> secular, into a "free and voluntary union", between persons who are social-and-legal equals; facilitated <a href="/wiki/Divorce" title="Divorce">divorce</a>; legalized <a href="/wiki/Abortion" title="Abortion">abortion</a>, eliminated <a href="/wiki/Bastardy" class="mw-redirect" title="Bastardy">bastardy</a> ("illegitimate children"); and voided the political power of the <a href="/wiki/Bourgeoisie" title="Bourgeoisie">bourgeoisie</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Private_property" title="Private property">private property</a>-status of the <a href="/wiki/Means_of_production" title="Means of production">means of production</a>. The educational system imparts the social norms for a self-disciplined and self-fulfilling way of life, by which the socialist citizens establish the social order necessary for realizing a communist society.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Marxist–Leninist cultural policy <a href="/wiki/Modernisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Modernisation">modernises</a> social relations among citizens by eliminating the capitalist value system of <a href="/wiki/Traditionalist_conservatism" title="Traditionalist conservatism">traditionalist conservatism</a>, by which Tsarism classified, divided, and controlled people with <a href="/wiki/Social_stratification" title="Social stratification">stratified social classes</a> without any socio-economic mobility. The socio-cultural changes required for establishing a communist society are realised with education and <a href="/wiki/Agitprop" title="Agitprop">agitprop</a> (agitation and propaganda), which reinforce communal values.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> The modernisation of educational and cultural policies eliminates the societal atomisation — <a href="/wiki/Anomie" title="Anomie">anomie</a> and <a href="/wiki/Social_alienation" title="Social alienation">social alienation</a> — caused by <a href="/wiki/Cultural_backwardness" title="Cultural backwardness">cultural backwardness</a>; thus Marxism–Leninism develops the <a href="/wiki/New_Soviet_man" title="New Soviet man">New Soviet man</a>, an educated and cultured citizen possessed of a proletarian <a href="/wiki/Class_consciousness" title="Class consciousness">class consciousness</a> who is oriented towards the <a href="/wiki/Collectivism" title="Collectivism">social cohesion</a> necessary for developing a communist society.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Church.E2.80.93State_relations"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Church–State_relations">Church–State relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marxism%E2%80%93Leninism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Church–State relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Christ_saviour_explosion.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Christ_saviour_explosion.jpg/300px-Christ_saviour_explosion.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="229" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Christ_saviour_explosion.jpg/450px-Christ_saviour_explosion.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Christ_saviour_explosion.jpg/600px-Christ_saviour_explosion.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="610" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Christ_saviour_explosion.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>In establishing <a href="/wiki/State_atheism" title="State atheism">official atheism</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Stalin" title="Joseph Stalin">Joseph Stalin</a> ordered in 1931 the razing of the <a href="/wiki/Cathedral_of_Christ_the_Saviour" title="Cathedral of Christ the Saviour">Cathedral of Christ the Saviour</a> in Moscow</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Marxist%E2%80%93Leninist_atheism" title="Marxist–Leninist atheism">Marxist–Leninist atheism</a></div>
<p>The Marxist–Leninist world view is <a href="/wiki/Atheism" title="Atheism">atheist</a>, wherein all human activity results from human <a href="/wiki/Volition_(psychology)" title="Volition (psychology)">volition</a>, and not the will of <a href="/wiki/Supernaturalism" class="mw-redirect" title="Supernaturalism">supernatural beings</a> (gods, goddesses, and demons) who have direct <a href="/wiki/Agency_(sociology)" title="Agency (sociology)">agency</a> in the public and private affairs of human society.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> The tenets of the Soviet Union's national policy of <a href="/wiki/Marxist%E2%80%93Leninist_atheism" title="Marxist–Leninist atheism">Marxist–Leninist atheism</a> originated from the philosophies of <a href="/wiki/Georg_Wilhelm_Friedrich_Hegel" title="Georg Wilhelm Friedrich Hegel">Georg Wilhelm Friedrich Hegel</a> (1770–1831) and <a href="/wiki/Ludwig_Feuerbach" title="Ludwig Feuerbach">Ludwig Feuerbach</a> (1804–1872), and of <a href="/wiki/Karl_Marx" title="Karl Marx">Karl Marx</a> (1818–1883) and <a href="/wiki/Lenin" class="mw-redirect" title="Lenin">Lenin</a> (1870–1924).<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As a basis of Marxism–Leninism, the philosophy of <a href="/wiki/Materialism" title="Materialism">materialism</a> (the <a href="/wiki/Universe" title="Universe">physical universe</a> exists independently of <a href="/wiki/Consciousness" title="Consciousness">human consciousness</a>) is applied as <a href="/wiki/Dialectical_materialism" title="Dialectical materialism">dialectical materialism</a> (a philosophy of science and <a href="/wiki/Nature" title="Nature">Nature</a>) to examine the socio-economic relations among people and things, as parts of a dynamic, material world that is unlike the immaterial world of <a href="/wiki/Metaphysics" title="Metaphysics">Metaphysics</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> The Soviet astrophysicist <a href="/wiki/Vitaly_Ginzburg" title="Vitaly Ginzburg">Vitaly Ginzburg</a> said that, ideologically, the "Bolshevik communists were not merely atheists, but, according to Lenin's terminology, <i>militant atheists</i>" in excluding religion from the social mainstream, from education, and from government.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International_relations">International relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marxism%E2%80%93Leninism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: International relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Marxist–Leninist approach to <a href="/wiki/International_relations" title="International relations">international relations</a> derives from the analyses (political and economic, sociological and geopolitical) that Lenin presented in the essay <i><a href="/wiki/Imperialism,_the_Highest_Stage_of_Capitalism" title="Imperialism, the Highest Stage of Capitalism">Imperialism, the Highest Stage of Capitalism</a> </i> (1917). Extrapolating from five philosophical bases of Marxism — (i) that human history is the history of <a href="/wiki/Class_struggle" class="mw-redirect" title="Class struggle">class struggle</a>, between a ruling class and an exploited class; (ii) that capitalism creates antagonistic <a href="/wiki/Social_class" title="Social class">social classes</a>: the <a href="/wiki/Bourgeoisie" title="Bourgeoisie">bourgeois exploiters</a> and the exploited <a href="/wiki/Proletariat" title="Proletariat">proletariat</a>; (iii) that capitalism employs <a href="/wiki/Nationalism" title="Nationalism">nationalist war</a> to further private economic expansion; (iv) that <a href="/wiki/Socialism" title="Socialism">socialism</a> is an economic system that voids social classes through <a href="/wiki/Public_ownership" class="mw-redirect" title="Public ownership">public ownership</a> of the means of production, and so will eliminate the economic causes of war; and (v) that once the state (<a href="/wiki/Socialist_state" title="Socialist state">socialist</a> or <a href="/wiki/Communist_state" title="Communist state">communist</a>) withers away, so shall international relations wither away, because they are projections of national economic forces — Lenin said that the capitalists' exhaustion of domestic sources of investment profit, by way of price-fixing <a href="/wiki/Trust_(business)" title="Trust (business)">trusts</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cartel" title="Cartel">cartels</a>, then prompts the same capitalists to export <a href="/wiki/Investment_capital" class="mw-redirect" title="Investment capital">investment capital</a> to undeveloped countries to finance the <a href="/wiki/Exploitation_of_natural_resources" title="Exploitation of natural resources">exploitation of natural resources</a> and the native populations, and to create new markets. That the capitalists' control of national politics ensures the government's military safeguarding of <a href="/wiki/Colonialism" title="Colonialism">colonial</a> investments, and the consequent imperial competition for economic supremacy provokes international wars to protect their national interests.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the vertical perspective (social-class relations) of Marxism–Leninism, the internal and international affairs of a country are a political continuum, not separate realms of human activity, which is the philosophic opposite of the horizontal perspectives (country-to-country) of the <a href="/wiki/Liberalism_(international_relations)" title="Liberalism (international relations)">liberal</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Realism_(international_relations)" title="Realism (international relations)">realist</a> approaches to international relations. Therefore, colonial imperialism is the inevitable consequence&#160; in the course of economic relations among countries when the domestic price-fixing of <a href="/wiki/Monopoly" title="Monopoly">monopoly capitalism</a> has voided profitable competition in the capitalist homeland. As such, the ideology of <a href="/wiki/New_Imperialism" title="New Imperialism">New Imperialism</a> — rationalised as a <a href="/wiki/Civilising_mission" class="mw-redirect" title="Civilising mission">civilising mission</a> — allowed the exportation of high-profit investment capital to undeveloped countries with uneducated, native populations (sources of cheap labour), plentiful raw materials for exploitation (factors for manufacture), and a colonial market to consume the <a href="/wiki/Surplus_production" class="mw-redirect" title="Surplus production">surplus production</a>, which the capitalist homeland cannot consume; the example is the European <a href="/wiki/Scramble_for_Africa" title="Scramble for Africa">Scramble for Africa</a> (1881–1914), which imperialism was safeguarded by the national military.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>To secure the economic and settler colonies — foreign sources of new capital-investment-profit — the imperialist state seeks either political or military control of the limited resources (natural and human); the First World War (1914–1918) resulted from such geopolitical conflicts among the empires of Europe over colonial <a href="/wiki/Sphere_of_influence" title="Sphere of influence">spheres of influence</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> For the colonised working classes who create the wealth (goods and services), the elimination of war for natural resources (access, control, and exploitation) is resolved by overthrowing the <a href="/wiki/Militarism" title="Militarism">militaristic</a> capitalist state and establishing a socialist state, because a peaceful world economy is feasible only by <a href="/wiki/Proletarian_revolution" title="Proletarian revolution">proletarian revolutions</a> that overthrow systems of <a href="/wiki/Political_economy" title="Political economy">political economy</a> based upon the <a href="/wiki/Exploitation_of_labour" title="Exploitation of labour">exploitation of labour</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_46-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marxism%E2%80%93Leninism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bolshevism">Bolshevism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marxism%E2%80%93Leninism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Bolshevism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The philosophy of Marxism–Leninism originated as the pro-active, political praxis of the Bolshevik (Majority) faction of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Social_Democratic_Labour_Party" title="Russian Social Democratic Labour Party">Russian Social Democratic Labour Party</a> (RSDLP) in realising political change in Tsarist Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> Lenin's leadership transformed the Bolsheviks into the RSDLP's political vanguard, which was composed of professional revolutionaries who practised <a href="/wiki/Democratic_centralism" title="Democratic centralism">democratic centralism</a> to elect leaders and officers, and to determine policy through free discussion, then decisively realised through united action.<sup id="cite_ref-freedomunity_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-freedomunity-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Vanguardism" title="Vanguardism">vanguardism</a> of pro-active, pragmatic commitment to achieving revolution was the Bolsheviks' advantage in out-manoeuvring the Liberal and Conservative political parties who advocated <a href="/wiki/Social_democracy" title="Social democracy">social democracy</a> without a practical plan of action for the Russian society they wished to govern; thus, <a href="/wiki/Leninism" title="Leninism">Leninism</a> allowed the Bolshevik Party to assume command of the <a href="/wiki/October_Revolution" title="October Revolution">October Revolution</a>, in 1917.<sup id="cite_ref-massaschussetts1991_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-massaschussetts1991-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="February_Revolution_.281905.E2.80.931907.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="February_Revolution_(1905–1907)">February Revolution (1905–1907)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marxism%E2%80%93Leninism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: February Revolution (1905–1907)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-H28740,_St._Petersburg,_Er%C3%B6ffnung_der_Parlamente.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-H28740%2C_St._Petersburg%2C_Er%C3%B6ffnung_der_Parlamente.jpg/300px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-H28740%2C_St._Petersburg%2C_Er%C3%B6ffnung_der_Parlamente.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="210" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-H28740%2C_St._Petersburg%2C_Er%C3%B6ffnung_der_Parlamente.jpg/450px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-H28740%2C_St._Petersburg%2C_Er%C3%B6ffnung_der_Parlamente.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-H28740%2C_St._Petersburg%2C_Er%C3%B6ffnung_der_Parlamente.jpg/600px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-H28740%2C_St._Petersburg%2C_Er%C3%B6ffnung_der_Parlamente.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="560" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-H28740,_St._Petersburg,_Er%C3%B6ffnung_der_Parlamente.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>In 1906, after the failed <a href="/wiki/1905_Russian_Revolution" title="1905 Russian Revolution">February Revolution of 1905</a>,  Tsar Nicholas II addressed the two chambers of the <a href="/wiki/State_Duma_(Russian_Empire)" title="State Duma (Russian Empire)">Duma</a>, at the Winter Palace</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:LeninEnSuizaMarzo1916--barbaroussovietr00mcbr.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/LeninEnSuizaMarzo1916--barbaroussovietr00mcbr.png/300px-LeninEnSuizaMarzo1916--barbaroussovietr00mcbr.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="409" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/4a/LeninEnSuizaMarzo1916--barbaroussovietr00mcbr.png 1.5x" data-file-width="387" data-file-height="527" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:LeninEnSuizaMarzo1916--barbaroussovietr00mcbr.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The failed February Revolution (1905–1907) against Tsar Nicholas II exiled Lenin from <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Russia" class="mw-redirect" title="Imperial Russia">Imperial Russia</a> to Switzerland in March 1905</div></div></div>
<p>Twelve years before the October Revolution in 1917, the Bolsheviks had failed to assume control of the <a href="/wiki/1905_Russian_Revolution" title="1905 Russian Revolution">February Revolution of 1905</a> (22 January 1905– 16 June 1907) because the centres of revolutionary action were too far apart for proper political co-ordination.<sup id="cite_ref-massaschussetts2_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-massaschussetts2-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> To generate revolutionary momentum — from the Tsarist army's killings on <a href="/wiki/Bloody_Sunday_(1905)" title="Bloody Sunday (1905)">Bloody Sunday</a> (22 January 1905) — the Bolsheviks advocated that workers use political violence to compel the bourgeois social classes (the nobility, the gentry, the bourgeoisie) to join the <a href="/wiki/Proletarian_revolution" title="Proletarian revolution">proletarian revolution</a> to overthrow the <a href="/wiki/Absolute_monarchy" title="Absolute monarchy">absolute monarchy</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Tsar_of_Russia" class="mw-redirect" title="Tsar of Russia">Tsar of Russia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Despite secret-police persecution by the <i><a href="/wiki/Okhrana" title="Okhrana">Okhrana</a></i> (Department for Protecting the Public Security and Order), émigré Bolsheviks returned to Russia to agitate, organise and lead; and then returned to exile when revolutionary fervour failed in 1907.<sup id="cite_ref-intellectual1965_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-intellectual1965-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> The failure of the February Revolution (1905–1907) exiled the Bolsheviks and the Mensheviks, the <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Revolutionary_Party" title="Socialist Revolutionary Party">Socialist Revolutionaries</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Black_Guards" title="Black Guards">Black Guard anarchists</a> from Russia — a political defeat aggravated by <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_II_of_Russia" title="Nicholas II of Russia">Tsar Nicholas II</a>'s political reformations of imperial Russian government. In practice, the formalities of political participation — the <a href="/wiki/State_Duma_(Russian_Empire)" title="State Duma (Russian Empire)">State Duma</a>, the political plurality of a <a href="/wiki/Multi-party_system" title="Multi-party system">multi-party system</a> of elections; and the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Constitution_of_1906" title="Russian Constitution of 1906">Russian Constitution of 1906</a> — were the Tsar's piecemeal and cosmetic concessions to <a href="/wiki/Social_progress" class="mw-redirect" title="Social progress">social progress</a>, which allowed public-office only the <a href="/wiki/Aristocracy_(class)" title="Aristocracy (class)">aristocracy</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Gentry" title="Gentry">gentry</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Bourgeoisie" title="Bourgeoisie">bourgeoisie</a>; but did not practically resolve the <a href="/wiki/Illiteracy" class="mw-redirect" title="Illiteracy">illiteracy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Poverty" title="Poverty">poverty</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Malnutrition" title="Malnutrition">malnutrition</a> of the proletarian majority of Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In Swiss exile, Lenin developed Marx's philosophy and extrapolated <a href="/wiki/Decolonisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Decolonisation">decolonisation</a>, by colonial revolt, as a reinforcement of <a href="/wiki/Proletarian_revolution" title="Proletarian revolution">proletarian revolution</a> in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-massaschussetts3_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-massaschussetts3-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> In 1912, Lenin resolved a factional challenge to his ideological leadership of the RSDLP by the Forward Group in the party, by usurping the all-party congress to transform the RSDLP into the <a href="/wiki/Bolshevik_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="Bolshevik Party">Bolshevik Party</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Great_War_.281914.E2.80.931918.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Great_War_(1914–1918)">Great War (1914–1918)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marxism%E2%80%93Leninism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Great War (1914–1918)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>As promised to the Russian peoples in October 1917, on 3 March 1918, the Bolsheviks quit Russia's participation in the <a href="/wiki/Great_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Great War">Great War</a> (1914–1918); unlike the European socialists who chose bellicose nationalism to anti-war internationalism; the philosophic and political break was consequence of the <a href="/wiki/Internationalist%E2%80%93defencist_schism" title="Internationalist–defencist schism">Internationalist–defencist schism</a> among Socialists.<sup id="cite_ref-university1995_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-university1995-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> That nationalist betrayal of socialism was denounced by a small group of socialist leaders who opposed the Great War, including <a href="/wiki/Rosa_Luxemburg" title="Rosa Luxemburg">Rosa Luxemburg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Karl_Liebknecht" title="Karl Liebknecht">Karl Liebknecht</a>, and Lenin, who said that the European socialists had failed the working classes, for preferring patriotic war to <a href="/wiki/Proletarian_internationalism" title="Proletarian internationalism">proletarian internationalism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-university1995_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-university1995-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> To debunk <a href="/wiki/Patriotism" title="Patriotism">patriotism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chauvinism" title="Chauvinism">national chauvinism</a>, in the essay <i><a href="/wiki/Imperialism,_the_Highest_Stage_of_Capitalism" title="Imperialism, the Highest Stage of Capitalism">Imperialism, the Highest Stage of Capitalism</a></i> (1917), Lenin explained that capitalist economic expansion leads to <a href="/wiki/Imperialism" title="Imperialism">colonial imperialism</a>, which then is regulated with nationalist wars — such as the Great War among the empires of Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Late in 1917 — to relieve strategic pressures from the <a href="/wiki/Western_Front_(World_War_I)" title="Western Front (World War I)">Western Front</a> (4 August 1914 – 11 November 1918) — <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Germany" class="mw-redirect" title="Imperial Germany">Imperial Germany</a> impelled the withdrawal of <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Russia" class="mw-redirect" title="Imperial Russia">Imperial Russia</a> from the war's <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Front_(World_War_I)" title="Eastern Front (World War I)">Eastern Front</a> (17 August 1914 – 3 March 1918) by sending Lenin and his Bolshevik cohort in a diplomatically-sealed train to realise socialist revolution in Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="October_Revolution_and_Russian_Civil_War_.281917.E2.80.931925.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="October_Revolution_and_Russian_Civil_War_(1917–1925)">October Revolution and Russian Civil War (1917–1925)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marxism%E2%80%93Leninism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: October Revolution and Russian Civil War (1917–1925)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Alfred_Grohs_zur_Revolution_1918_1919_in_Berlin_Gro%C3%9Fe_Frankfurter_Stra%C3%9Fe_Ecke_Lebuser_Stra%C3%9Fe_Barrikade_Kampf_w%C3%A4hrend_der_Novemberrevolution_in_Berlin_02_Bildseite_Schaulustige.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Alfred_Grohs_zur_Revolution_1918_1919_in_Berlin_Gro%C3%9Fe_Frankfurter_Stra%C3%9Fe_Ecke_Lebuser_Stra%C3%9Fe_Barrikade_Kampf_w%C3%A4hrend_der_Novemberrevolution_in_Berlin_02_Bildseite_Schaulustige.jpg/300px-thumbnail.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="466" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Alfred_Grohs_zur_Revolution_1918_1919_in_Berlin_Gro%C3%9Fe_Frankfurter_Stra%C3%9Fe_Ecke_Lebuser_Stra%C3%9Fe_Barrikade_Kampf_w%C3%A4hrend_der_Novemberrevolution_in_Berlin_02_Bildseite_Schaulustige.jpg/450px-thumbnail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Alfred_Grohs_zur_Revolution_1918_1919_in_Berlin_Gro%C3%9Fe_Frankfurter_Stra%C3%9Fe_Ecke_Lebuser_Stra%C3%9Fe_Barrikade_Kampf_w%C3%A4hrend_der_Novemberrevolution_in_Berlin_02_Bildseite_Schaulustige.jpg/600px-thumbnail.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2088" data-file-height="3240" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Alfred_Grohs_zur_Revolution_1918_1919_in_Berlin_Gro%C3%9Fe_Frankfurter_Stra%C3%9Fe_Ecke_Lebuser_Stra%C3%9Fe_Barrikade_Kampf_w%C3%A4hrend_der_Novemberrevolution_in_Berlin_02_Bildseite_Schaulustige.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>From 4 to 15 January 1919, the <a href="/wiki/Spartacist_uprising" title="Spartacist uprising">Spartacist uprising</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Weimar_Republic" title="Weimar Republic">Weimar Republic</a> featured <a href="/wiki/Urban_warfare" title="Urban warfare">urban warfare</a> between the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Germany" title="Communist Party of Germany">Communist Party of Germany</a> (KPD) and anti-communists, secretly aided by the Imperial German government led by the <a href="/wiki/Social_Democratic_Party_of_Germany" title="Social Democratic Party of Germany">Social Democratic Party of Germany</a> (SPD)</div></div></div>
<p>In March 1917, the abdication of Tsar Nicholas II led to the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Provisional_Government" title="Russian Provisional Government">Russian Provisional Government</a> (March–July 1917), who then proclaimed the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Republic" title="Russian Republic">Russian Republic</a> (September–November 1917). Later, in the <a href="/wiki/October_Revolution" title="October Revolution">October Revolution</a>, the Bolshevik's <i>coup d'état</i> against the Provisional Government resulted in their establishment of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Soviet_Federative_Socialist_Republic" title="Russian Soviet Federative Socialist Republic">Russian Soviet Federative Socialist Republic</a> (1917–1991); yet parts of Russia remained occupied by the counter-revolutionary <a href="/wiki/White_Movement" class="mw-redirect" title="White Movement">White Movement</a> of anti-communists who had united to form the <a href="/wiki/White_Army" class="mw-redirect" title="White Army">White Army</a> to fight the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Civil_War" title="Russian Civil War">Russian Civil War</a> (1917–1922) against the Bolshevik government.
</p><p>Despite the White–Red civil war, Russia remained a combatant in the Great War (1914–1918), which the Bolshevik's had quit with the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Brest-Litovsk" title="Treaty of Brest-Litovsk">Treaty of Brest-Litovsk</a> (3 March 1918), which then provoked the <a href="/wiki/Allied_intervention_in_the_Russian_Civil_War" title="Allied intervention in the Russian Civil War">Allied Intervention to the Russian Civil War</a> (1918–1925) by the armies of seventeen countries, featuring Great Britain, France, and Italy, the United States and Imperial Japan.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1918, the Bolsheviks consolidated government power by expelling the Mensheviks and the Socialist Revolutionaries from the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_(council)" title="Soviet (council)">soviets</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-dictatorships1918_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dictatorships1918-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> The Bolshevik government then established the <i><a href="/wiki/Cheka" title="Cheka">Cheka</a></i> secret police to eliminate anti–Bolshevik opposition in all the Russias. Initially, there was strong opposition to the Bolshevik régime, because they had not resolved the food shortages and material poverty of the Russian peoples, as promised in October 1917; from that social discontent, the Cheka reported 118 uprisings, including the <a href="/wiki/Kronstadt_rebellion" title="Kronstadt rebellion">Kronstadt rebellion</a> (7–17 March 1921).<sup id="cite_ref-dictatorships1918_62-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dictatorships1918-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dt>Nationalisation and War Communism</dt></dl>
<p>The Bolshevik government introduced limited <a href="/wiki/Nationalisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Nationalisation">nationalisation</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Means_of_production" title="Means of production">means of production</a>, which had been private property of the Russian aristocracy during the Tsarist monarchy.<sup id="cite_ref-dictatorships2_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dictatorships2-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> To fulfil the promised redistribution of Russia's arable land, Lenin encouraged the peasantry to reclaim their farmlands from the aristocrats and so ensured the peasantry's political loyalty to the Bolshevik Party.<sup id="cite_ref-dictatorships2_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dictatorships2-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> In mid-1918, to overcome the civil war's economic interruption, the <a href="/wiki/War_Communism" class="mw-redirect" title="War Communism">War Communism</a> policy featured a <a href="/wiki/Regulated_market" title="Regulated market">regulated market</a>, state-control of the means of distribution and the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Decree" title="Soviet Decree">Decree on Nationalisation</a> of large-scale farms, which requisitioned grain to feed industrial workers in the cities and the Red Army in the field, all while fighting the White Army, who was seeking to re-establish the <a href="/wiki/Romanov" class="mw-redirect" title="Romanov">Romanov</a> dynasty as <a href="/wiki/Absolute_monarchy" title="Absolute monarchy">absolute monarchs</a> of Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-dictatorships2_63-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dictatorships2-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> Politically, the forced grain-requisitions discouraged peasants from farming, which resulted in reduced-harvests and food-shortages, which in turn provoked labour strikes and food riots. With the economic chaos—caused by the Bolshevik government's voiding the monetary economy—the Russian people replaced with <a href="/wiki/Barter" title="Barter">barter</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Black_market" title="Black market">black market</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-dictatorships2_63-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dictatorships2-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dt>New Economic Policy</dt></dl>
<p>In 1921, the <a href="/wiki/New_Economic_Policy" title="New Economic Policy">New Economic Policy</a> restored some private enterprise to animate the Russian economy. As part of Lenin's pragmatic compromise with external financial interests in 1918, Bolshevik <a href="/wiki/State_capitalism" title="State capitalism">state capitalism</a> temporarily returned 91 per cent of industry to private ownership—until the Soviet Russians learned to operate and administrate said industries.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-dictatorships2_63-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dictatorships2-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> In that vein, Lenin explained that developing socialism in Russia would proceed according to the material and socio-economic conditions of Russia and not as described by Marx in the 19th century. Lenin's pragmatic explanation was the following: "Our poverty is so great that we cannot, at one stroke, restore full-scale factory, state, socialist production".<sup id="cite_ref-dictatorships2_63-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dictatorships2-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> To overcome the lack of educated Russians who could operate and administrate industry, Lenin advocated the development of a <a href="/wiki/Intelligentsia" title="Intelligentsia">technical intelligentsia</a> who would propel the industrial development of Russia to self-sufficiency.<sup id="cite_ref-massaschussetts2_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-massaschussetts2-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bela.Kun.Revolution.1919.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Bela.Kun.Revolution.1919.jpg/300px-Bela.Kun.Revolution.1919.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="200" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Bela.Kun.Revolution.1919.jpg/450px-Bela.Kun.Revolution.1919.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Bela.Kun.Revolution.1919.jpg/600px-Bela.Kun.Revolution.1919.jpg 2x" data-file-width="740" data-file-height="494" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bela.Kun.Revolution.1919.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/B%C3%A9la_Kun" title="Béla Kun">Béla Kun</a>, leader of the <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_Soviet_Republic" title="Hungarian Soviet Republic">Hungarian Soviet Republic</a>, speaks to supporters during the <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_Revolution_of_1919" class="mw-redirect" title="Hungarian Revolution of 1919">Hungarian Revolution of 1919</a></div></div></div>
<p>The principal obstacles to Russian economic development and modernisation were great <a href="/wiki/Poverty" title="Poverty">material poverty</a> and the lack of modern technology, which conditions <a href="/wiki/Orthodox_Marxism" title="Orthodox Marxism">orthodox Marxism</a> considered unfavourable to communist revolution; and that agricultural Russia was right for developing capitalism, but wrong for the development of socialism.<sup id="cite_ref-massaschussetts2_51-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-massaschussetts2-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> The 1921–1924 period was tumultuous in Russia, with the simultaneous occurrence of economic recovery, famine (1921–1922) and a financial crisis (1924).<sup id="cite_ref-dictatorships3_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dictatorships3-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> By 1924, the Bolshevik government had achieved much economic progress and by 1926 the production levels of the Soviet Union's economy had risen to the production levels registered in 1913.<sup id="cite_ref-dictatorships3_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dictatorships3-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dt>Revolutionary consequences</dt></dl>
<p>Elsewhere, the successful <a href="/wiki/October_Revolution" title="October Revolution">October Revolution</a> in Russia facilitated the <a href="/wiki/German_Revolution_of_1918%E2%80%9319" class="mw-redirect" title="German Revolution of 1918–19">German Revolution of 1918–19</a> and <a href="/wiki/Revolutions_and_interventions_in_Hungary_(1918%E2%80%9320)" title="Revolutions and interventions in Hungary (1918–20)">Revolutions and interventions in Hungary (1918–20)</a> which produced the <a href="/wiki/First_Hungarian_Republic" title="First Hungarian Republic">First Hungarian Republic</a> (1918–1919) and the <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_Soviet_Republic" title="Hungarian Soviet Republic">Hungarian Soviet Republic</a> (March–August 1919). In Berlin, the German government and their <i><a href="/wiki/Freikorps" title="Freikorps">Freikorps</a></i> mercenaries fought and defeated the <a href="/wiki/Spartacist_uprising" title="Spartacist uprising">Spartacist uprising</a> (4–5 January 1919), which began as a <a href="/wiki/General_strike" title="General strike">general strike</a>; and likewise, the local Freikorps in Munich fought and defeated the <a href="/wiki/Bavarian_Soviet_Republic" title="Bavarian Soviet Republic">Bavarian Soviet Republic</a> (April 1919). In Hungary, the disorganised workers who had proclaimed the Hungarian Soviet Republic were fought and defeated by the royal armies of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Romania" title="Kingdom of Romania">Kingdom of Romania</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Yugoslavia" title="Kingdom of Yugoslavia">Kingdom of Yugoslavia</a> and the army of the <a href="/wiki/First_Republic_of_Czechoslovakia" class="mw-redirect" title="First Republic of Czechoslovakia">First Republic of Czechoslovakia</a>. In Asia, the successful <a href="/wiki/Mongolian_Revolution_of_1921" title="Mongolian Revolution of 1921">Mongolian Revolution of 1921</a> established the <a href="/wiki/Mongolian_People%27s_Republic" title="Mongolian People&#39;s Republic">Mongolian People's Republic</a> (1924–1992).
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Stalin_assumes_power">Stalin assumes power</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marxism%E2%80%93Leninism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Stalin assumes power">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Vladimir_Lenin_on_the_front_page_of_Projector_(Spotlight)_issue_15_dated_15_Sep_1923.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Vladimir_Lenin_on_the_front_page_of_Projector_%28Spotlight%29_issue_15_dated_15_Sep_1923.jpg/300px-Vladimir_Lenin_on_the_front_page_of_Projector_%28Spotlight%29_issue_15_dated_15_Sep_1923.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="430" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Vladimir_Lenin_on_the_front_page_of_Projector_%28Spotlight%29_issue_15_dated_15_Sep_1923.jpg/450px-Vladimir_Lenin_on_the_front_page_of_Projector_%28Spotlight%29_issue_15_dated_15_Sep_1923.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Vladimir_Lenin_on_the_front_page_of_Projector_%28Spotlight%29_issue_15_dated_15_Sep_1923.jpg/600px-Vladimir_Lenin_on_the_front_page_of_Projector_%28Spotlight%29_issue_15_dated_15_Sep_1923.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1973" data-file-height="2826" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Vladimir_Lenin_on_the_front_page_of_Projector_(Spotlight)_issue_15_dated_15_Sep_1923.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>At his death on 21 January 1924, <a href="/wiki/Lenin%27s_Testament" title="Lenin&#39;s Testament">Lenin's political testament</a> ordered the removal of Stalin as <a href="/wiki/General_Secretary_of_the_Communist_Party_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="General Secretary of the Communist Party of the Soviet Union">General Secretary of the Communist Party of the Soviet Union</a> because of his abusive personality</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Stalin-Bukharin_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Stalin-Bukharin_%28cropped%29.jpg/300px-Stalin-Bukharin_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="225" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Stalin-Bukharin_%28cropped%29.jpg/450px-Stalin-Bukharin_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/ee/Stalin-Bukharin_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="460" data-file-height="345" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Stalin-Bukharin_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>To expel <a href="/wiki/Leon_Trotsky" title="Leon Trotsky">Leon Trotsky</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Communist Party of the Soviet Union">Communist Party</a>, Stalin and <a href="/wiki/Nikolai_Bukharin" title="Nikolai Bukharin">Nikolai Bukharin</a> expediently joined forces to achieve Stalin's control of the Communist Party</div></div></div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r889293853/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{text-align:left;background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style>
<dl><dt>Lenin's warning</dt></dl>
<p>In his <a href="/wiki/Lenin%27s_testament" class="mw-redirect" title="Lenin&#39;s testament">political testament</a> (December 1922), Lenin ordered Stalin removed from being the <a href="/wiki/General_Secretary_of_the_Communist_Party_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="General Secretary of the Communist Party of the Soviet Union">General Secretary</a> of the Russian Communist Party, and that he be replaced with "some other person who is superior to Stalin only in one respect, namely, in being more tolerant, more loyal, more polite, and more attentive to comrades."<sup id="cite_ref-dictatorships4_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dictatorships4-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> At his death on 21 January 1924, Lenin's testament was read aloud to the Central Committee, but enough members believed that Stalin had been politically rehabilitated in 1923, and ignored Lenin's order to remove Stalin as General Secretary of the Communist Party.<sup id="cite_ref-dictatorships4_67-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dictatorships4-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-dictatorships5_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dictatorships5-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dt>Power struggle</dt></dl>
