<p>Consequent to personally spiteful disputes about the praxis of <a href="/wiki/Leninism" title="Leninism">Leninism</a>, the October Revolution veterans <a href="/wiki/Lev_Kamenev" title="Lev Kamenev">Lev Kamenev</a> and <a href="/wiki/Grigory_Zinoviev" title="Grigory Zinoviev">Grigory Zinoviev</a> said that the true, ideological threat to the ideological integrity of the Communist Party was Trotsky, who was a personally charismatic political-leader; the commanding officer of the <a href="/wiki/Red_Army" title="Red Army">Red Army</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Civil_War" title="Russian Civil War">Russian Civil War</a>; and revolutionary partner of the dead Lenin.<sup id="cite_ref-dictatorships5_69-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dictatorships5-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> To thwart Trotsky's likely election to head the Communist Party, Stalin, Kamenev, and Zinoviev formed a <i><a href="/wiki/Triumvirate" title="Triumvirate">Troika</a></i> (Triumvirate) that featured Stalin as General Secretary of the Communist Party, the <i>de facto</i> <a href="/wiki/Power_(social_and_political)" title="Power (social and political)">centre of power</a> in the party and the country.<sup id="cite_ref-dictatorships6_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dictatorships6-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The direction of the Russian Communist Party was decided in confrontations of politics and personality — between Stalin's <i>Troika</i> and Trotsky — over which Marxist policy to pursue, either Trotsky's policy of <a href="/wiki/Permanent_revolution" title="Permanent revolution">permanent revolution</a> or Stalin's policy of <a href="/wiki/Socialism_in_One_Country" title="Socialism in One Country">Socialism in One Country</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-dictatorships7_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dictatorships7-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>&#160; To politically isolate and oust Trotsky from the Party, Stalin expediently advocated socialism in one country, a policy to which he was indifferent.<sup id="cite_ref-dictatorships7_71-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dictatorships7-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> In 1925, the <a href="/wiki/14th_Communist_Party_Congress" class="mw-redirect" title="14th Communist Party Congress">14th Communist Party Congress</a> chose Stalin's policy, which decision defeated Trotsky as a possible leader of the Communist Party and of the Soviet Union.<sup id="cite_ref-dictatorships7_71-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dictatorships7-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the 1925–1927 period, Stalin dissolved the <i>Troika</i> and disowned the centrist moderates, Kamenev and Zinoviev, for an expedient alliance with the three most-right-wing opportunists from the Bolshevik period: <a href="/wiki/Alexei_Rykov" title="Alexei Rykov">Alexei Rykov</a> (Premier of Russia, 1924–1929; Premier of the Soviet Union, 1924–1930),<sup id="cite_ref-Rykov_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rykov-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Nikolai_Bukharin" title="Nikolai Bukharin">Nikolai Bukharin</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Tomsky" title="Mikhail Tomsky">Mikhail Tomsky</a> (leader of the All-Russian Central Council of Trade Unions).<sup id="cite_ref-dictatorships7_71-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dictatorships7-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> In 1927, the Communist Party endorsed Stalin's policy of Socialism in One Country as the Soviet Union's national policy, and expelled the leftist Trotsky and the centrists Kamenev and Zinoviev from the <a href="/wiki/Politburo_of_the_Communist_Party_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Politburo of the Communist Party of the Soviet Union">Politburo of the Communist Party of the Soviet Union</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-dictatorships7_71-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dictatorships7-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dt>Power consolidated</dt></dl>
<p>In 1929, Stalin personally and politically controlled the CPSU and the Soviet Union, by way of deception and administrative acumen.<sup id="cite_ref-dictatorships7_71-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dictatorships7-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> In that time, Stalin's centralised, socialism-in-one-country régime had negatively associated Lenin's revolutionary <a href="/wiki/Bolshevism" class="mw-redirect" title="Bolshevism">Bolshevism</a> with Stalinism — government by command-policy to realise projects, such as the rapid industrialisation of cities and the collectivisation of agriculture; such Stalinism also subordinated the interests (political, national, ideologic) of Asian and European communist parties to the geopolitical interests of the Soviet Union.<sup id="cite_ref-massaschussetts1991_50-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-massaschussetts1991-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the 1929–1932 period of the <a href="/wiki/First_five-year_plan" title="First five-year plan">first five-year plan</a>, Stalin effected the <a href="/wiki/Dekulakization" title="Dekulakization">dekulakization</a> of the farmlands of the Soviet Union, a politically radical dispossession of the <i><a href="/wiki/Kulak" title="Kulak">kulak</a></i> class of peasant-landlords from the <a href="/wiki/Tsarism" class="mw-redirect" title="Tsarism">Tsarist</a> social order of monarchy. As old-school Bolshevik revolutionaries, Bukharin, Rykov, and Tomsky recommended amelioration of the dekulakization, to lessen the negative social impact in the relations between the Soviet peoples and the CPSU; Stalin took umbrage, and then accused them of un-communist philosophic deviations from Lenin and Marx.<sup id="cite_ref-dictatorships7_71-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dictatorships7-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>That implicit accusation of <a href="/wiki/Deviationism" title="Deviationism">ideological deviationism</a> licensed Stalin to falsely accuse Bukharin, Rykov, and Tomsky of plotting against the CPSU; the appearance of impropriety then compelled the resignations of the <a href="/wiki/Old_Bolsheviks" class="mw-redirect" title="Old Bolsheviks">Old Bolsheviks</a> from government and from the politburo. Stalin then completed his political purging of the Communist Party by <a href="/wiki/Exile" title="Exile">exiling</a> Trotsky from the Soviet Union in 1929;<sup id="cite_ref-dictatorships7_71-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dictatorships7-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> afterwards, In the political opposition to the practical régime of Stalinism was denounced as <a href="/wiki/Trotskyism" title="Trotskyism">Trotskyism</a> (Bolshevik–Leninism), a deviation from Marxism–Leninism, the state ideology of the Soviet Union.<sup id="cite_ref-massaschussetts1991_50-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-massaschussetts1991-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dt>Power legalised</dt></dl>
<p>In the 1929–1941 period, Stalin's elimination of <a href="/wiki/Old_Bolshevik" title="Old Bolshevik">Old Bolshevik</a> rivals ended <a href="/wiki/Democratic_centralism" title="Democratic centralism">democratic centralism</a> in the Communist Party, replaced with his personal authority.<sup id="cite_ref-dictatorships9_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dictatorships9-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> The ranks and files of the CPSU were populated with members from the trade unions and the factories, whom Stalin controlled because there were no other Old Bolsheviks to contradict Marxism–Leninism, Stalin's version of <a href="/wiki/Communism" title="Communism">Communism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-dictatorships9_73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dictatorships9-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> In the late 1930s, the Soviet Union adopted the <a href="/wiki/1936_Soviet_Constitution" class="mw-redirect" title="1936 Soviet Constitution">1936 Soviet Constitution</a>, which ended weighted-voting preferences for workers, promulgated <a href="/wiki/Universal_suffrage" title="Universal suffrage">universal suffrage</a> for every man and woman older than 18 years of age, and organised the soviets (councils of workers) into two legislatures: (i) the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_of_the_Union" title="Soviet of the Union">Soviet of the Union</a> (representing electoral districts) and (ii) the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_of_Nationalities" title="Soviet of Nationalities">Soviet of Nationalities</a> (representing the ethnic groups of the country).<sup id="cite_ref-dictatorships9_73-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dictatorships9-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dt>Dictator of the Soviet Union</dt></dl>
<p>Under guise of governing by the socialist principles of Lenin and Marx, Stalin's Marxist–Leninist dictatorship made a <a href="/wiki/Police_state" title="Police state">police state</a> of the USSR, unlike Lenin's <a href="/wiki/Socialist_state" title="Socialist state">socialist state</a> of the Bolshevik period (1917–29).<sup id="cite_ref-dictatorships8_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dictatorships8-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> Extensive personal control of the men who were the Communist Party licensed Stalin to use <a href="/wiki/Political_violence" title="Political violence">political violence</a> to eliminate any man or woman who might be a threat — real, potential, or imagined.<sup id="cite_ref-dictatorships8_74-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dictatorships8-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As an administrator, Stalin governed the Soviet Union by controlling the formulation of national policy, but delegated implementation to subordinate functionaries. Such freedom of action allowed local communist functionaries much discretion to interpret the intent of orders from Moscow, which allowed their corruption.<sup id="cite_ref-dictatorships8_74-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dictatorships8-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> To Stalin, the correction of such abuses of authority and economic corruption were responsibility of the secret police, the <a href="/wiki/NKVD" title="NKVD">NKVD</a> (People's Commissariat for Internal Affairs).<sup id="cite_ref-dictatorships8_74-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dictatorships8-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> With the <a href="/wiki/Great_Purge" title="Great Purge">Great Purge</a> (1936–1938), Stalin rid himself of internal enemies in the CPSU, and rid the Soviet Union of every counter-revolutionary, reactionary, and socially-dangerous man and woman who might offer legitimate, political opposition to Marxism–Leninism.
</p><p>In the 1937–1938 period, the NKVD arrested 1.5 million people, purged from every stratum of soviet society and every rank and file of the Communist Party, of which 681,692 people were killed as <a href="/wiki/Enemy_of_the_state" title="Enemy of the state">enemies of the state</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> To provide manpower (manual, intellectual, technical) to realise the construction of socialism in one country, the NKVD established the <i><a href="/wiki/Gulag" title="Gulag">Gulag</a></i> system of <a href="/wiki/Forced_labour" class="mw-redirect" title="Forced labour">forced-labour</a> camps for regular criminals and political dissidents, for culturally insubordinate artists and politically incorrect intellectuals, and for homosexual people and religious <a href="/wiki/Anti-communism" title="Anti-communism">anti-communists</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-dictatorships9_73-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dictatorships9-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Socialism_in_one_country_.281929.E2.80.931941.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Socialism_in_one_country_(1929–1941)">Socialism in one country (1929–1941)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marxism%E2%80%93Leninism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Socialism in one country (1929–1941)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-R85625,_Sowjetunion,_H%C3%BCttenkombinat_in_Magnitogorsk.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-R85625%2C_Sowjetunion%2C_H%C3%BCttenkombinat_in_Magnitogorsk.jpg/300px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-R85625%2C_Sowjetunion%2C_H%C3%BCttenkombinat_in_Magnitogorsk.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="440" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-R85625%2C_Sowjetunion%2C_H%C3%BCttenkombinat_in_Magnitogorsk.jpg/450px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-R85625%2C_Sowjetunion%2C_H%C3%BCttenkombinat_in_Magnitogorsk.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/cb/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-R85625%2C_Sowjetunion%2C_H%C3%BCttenkombinat_in_Magnitogorsk.jpg 2x" data-file-width="546" data-file-height="800" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-R85625,_Sowjetunion,_H%C3%BCttenkombinat_in_Magnitogorsk.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The metallurgical combine in <a href="/wiki/Magnitogorsk" title="Magnitogorsk">Magnitogorsk</a> in 1929 demonstrates the <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Soviet_Union_(1927%E2%80%931953)#History_of_the_Soviet_Union_(1927–1953)#Soviet_state&#39;s_development" title="History of the Soviet Union (1927–1953)">Soviet Union's rapid industrialisation in the 1920s and 1930s</a></div></div></div>
<dl><dt>Rapid industrialisation</dt></dl>
<p>Begun in 1928, Stalin's <a href="/wiki/Five-year_plans_for_the_national_economy_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Five-year plans for the national economy of the Soviet Union">Five-year plans for the national economy of the Soviet Union</a> achieved the rapid industrialisation (coal, iron, and steel, electricity and petroleum, etc.) and the collectivisation of agriculture,<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> which achieved 23.6 per cent collectivisation within one year (1930) and 98.0 per cent collectivisation within 12 years (1941).<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> The five-year plans were prepared in the 1920s, whilst the Bolshevik government fought the internal Russian Civil War (1917–1922) and repelled the external Allied intervention to the Russian Civil War (1918–1925). As the revolutionary vanguard, the Communist Party organised Russian society to realise rapid industrialisation programs as defence against Western interference with socialism in Bolshevik Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During the 1930s, the rapid industrialisation of the country accelerated the Russians' sociological transition from poverty to relative plenty; from Tsarist <a href="/wiki/Serfdom" title="Serfdom">serfdom</a> to Communist self-determination, when politically illiterate peasants became politically aware urban citizens.<sup id="cite_ref-dictatorships11_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dictatorships11-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> The Marxist–Leninist economic régime modernised Russia from the illiterate, peasant society characteristic of monarchy to the <a href="/wiki/Literacy" title="Literacy">literate</a>, socialist society of educated farmers and industrial workers; the modernisation of Russia reduced unemployment to almost nil.<sup id="cite_ref-dictatorships11_79-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dictatorships11-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dt>Social engineering</dt></dl>
<p>In 1934, Stalin's development of Soviet society contradicted and then replaced, the social, cultural, and intellectual freedoms of Lenin's Bolshevik period. In education, Socialist progress was replaced with traditional Russian <a href="/wiki/Authoritarianism" title="Authoritarianism">authoritarianism</a> (harsh discipline, school uniforms, etc.), which suppressed <a href="/wiki/Pedagogy" title="Pedagogy">pedagogic</a> experimentation and relaxed social conduct in the education of children; mental conformity, rather than intellectual liberty.<sup id="cite_ref-dictatorships10_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dictatorships10-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> Culturally, the Russian arts were subordinated to the ideological limitations of <a href="/wiki/Socialist_realism" title="Socialist realism">socialist realism</a>, a form of Russian <a href="/wiki/Patriarchy" title="Patriarchy">patriarchy</a> admired by the <a href="/wiki/Traditionalist_conservatism" title="Traditionalist conservatism">traditionalist</a> Stalin.<sup id="cite_ref-dictatorships10_80-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dictatorships10-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> The official atheism of the Soviet Union excluded organised religion from the mainstream of Soviet society and repressed any religious organisation that publicly participated in politics and opposed the official atheism.<sup id="cite_ref-dictatorships10_80-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dictatorships10-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dt>International relations</dt></dl>
<p>In 1933, the Marxist–Leninist geopolitical perspective was that the Soviet Union was surrounded by capitalist and anti-communist enemies; thus, the election of <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">Adolf Hitler</a> and his <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Party" title="Nazi Party">Nazi Party</a> government in Germany initially caused the Soviet Union to sever diplomatic relations that had been established in the 1920s. In 1938, Stalin accommodated the Nazis and the anti-communist West by not defending Czechoslovakia, which allowed Hitler's threat of pre-emptive war for the <a href="/wiki/Sudetenland" title="Sudetenland">Sudetenland</a> to annex the land and "rescue the oppressed German peoples" living in Czecho.<sup id="cite_ref-dictatorships12_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dictatorships12-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>To challenge <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a>'s bid for European empire and hegemony, Stalin promoted <a href="/wiki/Anti-fascism" title="Anti-fascism">anti-fascist</a> front organisations to encourage European socialists and democrats to join the Russian Communists to fight throughout Nazi-occupied Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-dictatorships12_81-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dictatorships12-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> After Germany bluffed Britain into the <a href="/wiki/Munich_Agreement" title="Munich Agreement">Munich Agreement</a> (29 September 1938), which then allowed the <a href="/wiki/German_occupation_of_Czechoslovakia" title="German occupation of Czechoslovakia">German occupation of Czechoslovakia</a> (1938–1945), Stalin adopted pro-German policies for the Soviet Union's dealings with Nazi Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-dictatorships12_81-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dictatorships12-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> In 1939, the Soviet Union and Nazi Germany agreed to the <a href="/wiki/Molotov%E2%80%93Ribbentrop_Pact" title="Molotov–Ribbentrop Pact">Treaty of Non-aggression between Germany and the Union of Soviet Socialist Republics</a> (Molotov–Ribbentrop Pact, 23 August 1939) and to jointly <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Poland" title="Invasion of Poland">invade and partition Poland</a>, by way of which Nazi Germany started the Second World War (1 September 1939).<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Great_Patriotic_War_.281941.E2.80.931945.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Great_Patriotic_War_(1941–1945)">Great Patriotic War (1941–1945)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marxism%E2%80%93Leninism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Great Patriotic War (1941–1945)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Long-march.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Long-march.jpg/300px-Long-march.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="159" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Long-march.jpg/450px-Long-march.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/49/Long-march.jpg 2x" data-file-width="585" data-file-height="310" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Long-march.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Communist_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="Chinese Communist Party">Chinese Communist Party</a> cadre-leader addresses survivors of the 1934–1935 <a href="/wiki/Long_March" title="Long March">Long March</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Yalta_Conference_(Churchill,_Roosevelt,_Stalin)_(B%26W).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Yalta_Conference_%28Churchill%2C_Roosevelt%2C_Stalin%29_%28B%26W%29.jpg/300px-Yalta_Conference_%28Churchill%2C_Roosevelt%2C_Stalin%29_%28B%26W%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="247" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Yalta_Conference_%28Churchill%2C_Roosevelt%2C_Stalin%29_%28B%26W%29.jpg/450px-Yalta_Conference_%28Churchill%2C_Roosevelt%2C_Stalin%29_%28B%26W%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Yalta_Conference_%28Churchill%2C_Roosevelt%2C_Stalin%29_%28B%26W%29.jpg/600px-Yalta_Conference_%28Churchill%2C_Roosevelt%2C_Stalin%29_%28B%26W%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2720" data-file-height="2239" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Yalta_Conference_(Churchill,_Roosevelt,_Stalin)_(B%26W).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>At the <a href="/wiki/Yalta_Conference" title="Yalta Conference">Yalta Conference</a> (4–11 February 1945), <a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">Winston Churchill</a>, <a href="/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt" title="Franklin D. Roosevelt">Franklin D. Roosevelt</a> and Stalin established the <a href="/wiki/Aftermath_of_World_War_II" title="Aftermath of World War II">post-war order of the world</a> with geopolitical <a href="/wiki/Spheres_of_influence" class="mw-redirect" title="Spheres of influence">spheres of influence</a> under their <a href="/wiki/Hegemony" title="Hegemony">hegemony</a></div></div></div>
<p>In the 1941–1942 period of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Patriotic_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Great Patriotic War">Great Patriotic War</a>, the <a href="/wiki/German_invasion_of_the_Soviet_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="German invasion of the Soviet Union">German invasion of the Soviet Union</a> (Operation Barbarossa, 22 June 1941) was ineffectively opposed by the <a href="/wiki/Red_Army" title="Red Army">Red Army</a>, who were poorly led, ill-trained, and under-equipped; hence fought poorly and suffered great losses of soldiers (killed, wounded, and captured). The weakness of the Red Army was consequence of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Purge" title="Great Purge">Great Purge</a> (1936–1938) of senior officers and career soldiers whom Stalin considered politically unreliable.<sup id="cite_ref-dictatorships13_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dictatorships13-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> Strategically, the <i><a href="/wiki/Wehrmacht" title="Wehrmacht">Wehrmacht</a>'</i>s extensive and effective attack threatened the territorial integrity of the Soviet Union, and the political integrity of Stalin's model of a Marxist–Leninist state, when the Nazis were initially welcomed as liberators by the anti-communist and nationalist populations in the <a href="/wiki/Byelorussian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Byelorussian Soviet Socialist Republic">Byelorussian Soviet Socialist Republic</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Georgian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Georgian Soviet Socialist Republic">Georgian Soviet Socialist Republic</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Ukrainian Soviet Socialist Republic">Ukrainian Soviet Socialist Republic</a>.
</p><p>The anti-soviet nationalists' <a href="/wiki/Collaborationism" title="Collaborationism">collaboration</a> with the Nazi's lasted until the <i><a href="/wiki/SS" class="mw-redirect" title="SS">SS</a></i> and the <i><a href="/wiki/Einsatzgruppen" title="Einsatzgruppen">Einsatzgruppen</a></i> began their <i><a href="/wiki/Lebensraum" title="Lebensraum">Lebensraum</a></i> killings of the Jewish populations, the local communists, the civil and community leaders — the <a href="/wiki/Holocaust" class="mw-redirect" title="Holocaust">Holocaust</a> meant to realise the Nazi German colonisation of Bolshevik Russia. In response, Stalin ordered the Red Army to fight a <a href="/wiki/Total_war" title="Total war">total war</a> against the Germanic invaders who would exterminate Slavic Russia. Hitler's attack against the Soviet Union (Nazi Germany's erstwhile ally) realigned Stalin's political priorities, from the repression of internal enemies to the existential defence against external attack. The pragmatic Stalin then entered the Soviet Union to the <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Grand Alliance</a>, in common front against the <a href="/wiki/Axis_Powers" class="mw-redirect" title="Axis Powers">Axis Powers</a> — Nazi Germany, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Italy_under_Fascism_(1922%E2%80%931943)" class="mw-redirect" title="Kingdom of Italy under Fascism (1922–1943)">Fascist Italy</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Japan" class="mw-redirect" title="Imperial Japan">Imperial Japan</a>.
</p><p>In the continental European countries occupied by the <a href="/wiki/Axis_powers" title="Axis powers">Axis powers</a>, the native communist party usually led the armed resistance (<a href="/wiki/Guerrilla_warfare" title="Guerrilla warfare">guerrilla warfare</a> and <a href="/wiki/Urban_guerrilla_warfare" title="Urban guerrilla warfare">urban guerrilla warfare</a>) against fascist military occupation. In Mediterranean Europe, the Communist <a href="/wiki/Yugoslav_Partisans" title="Yugoslav Partisans">Yugoslav Partisans</a>, led by Tito (<a href="/wiki/Josip_Broz" class="mw-redirect" title="Josip Broz">Josip Broz</a>), effectively resisted the Nazi and Fascist occupation. In the 1943–1944 period, Tito's Partisans liberated territories with Red Army assistance and established the Communist political authority that became the <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Federal_Republic_of_Yugoslavia" title="Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia">Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia</a>. In continental Asia, to end the Imperial Japanese occupation of China, Stalin ordered Mao Zedong and the Communist Party of China (CPC) to temporarily cease the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Civil_War" title="Chinese Civil War">Chinese Civil War</a> (1927–1949) against Chiang Kai-shek and the anti-communist Kuomintang (KMT), as the <a href="/wiki/Second_United_Front" title="Second United Front">Second United Front</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/Second_Sino-Japanese_War" title="Second Sino-Japanese War">Second Sino-Japanese War</a> (1937–1945).
</p>
<dl><dt>Communist victory</dt></dl>
<p>In 1943, the Red Army began to repel the Nazi invasion of the Soviet Union, especially at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Stalingrad" title="Battle of Stalingrad">Battle of Stalingrad</a> (23 August 1942 – 2 February 1943) and at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Kursk" title="Battle of Kursk">Battle of Kursk</a> (5 July – 23 August 1943). Then repelled the Nazi and Fascist occupation armies from Eastern Europe until the Red Army decisively defeated Nazi Germany, in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Berlin" title="Battle of Berlin">Berlin Strategic Offensive Operation</a> (16 April–2 May 1945).<sup id="cite_ref-dictatorships14_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dictatorships14-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> On concluding the Great Patriotic War (1941–1945), the Soviet Union was a military superpower with a say in determining the geopolitical order of the world.<sup id="cite_ref-dictatorships14_84-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dictatorships14-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> In accordance with the three-power <a href="/wiki/Yalta_Agreement" class="mw-redirect" title="Yalta Agreement">Yalta Agreement</a> (4–11 February 1945), the Soviet Union purged <a href="/wiki/Collaborationism" title="Collaborationism">native fascist collaborators</a> from the Eastern European countries occupied by the Axis Powers, and installed native Communist governments to establish a geographic buffer-zone of <a href="/wiki/Satellite_state" title="Satellite state">satellite states</a> to protect the borders of the USSR.
</p>
<h3><span id="Cold_War_.281945.E2.80.931991.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Cold_War_(1945–1991)">Cold War (1945–1991)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marxism%E2%80%93Leninism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Cold War (1945–1991)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mao_proclaiming_the_establishment_of_the_PRC_in_1949.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Mao_proclaiming_the_establishment_of_the_PRC_in_1949.jpg/300px-Mao_proclaiming_the_establishment_of_the_PRC_in_1949.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="232" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f2/Mao_proclaiming_the_establishment_of_the_PRC_in_1949.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="414" data-file-height="320" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mao_proclaiming_the_establishment_of_the_PRC_in_1949.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Communist_Revolution" title="Chinese Communist Revolution">Chinese Communist Revolution</a> (1946–1949) concluded when <a href="/wiki/Mao_Zedong" title="Mao Zedong">Mao Zedong</a> declared the establishment of the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="People&#39;s Republic of China">People's Republic of China</a> on 1 October 1949.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:John_Kennedy,_Nikita_Khrushchev_1961.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/John_Kennedy%2C_Nikita_Khrushchev_1961.jpg/300px-John_Kennedy%2C_Nikita_Khrushchev_1961.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="233" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/John_Kennedy%2C_Nikita_Khrushchev_1961.jpg/450px-John_Kennedy%2C_Nikita_Khrushchev_1961.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/John_Kennedy%2C_Nikita_Khrushchev_1961.jpg/600px-John_Kennedy%2C_Nikita_Khrushchev_1961.jpg 2x" data-file-width="760" data-file-height="590" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:John_Kennedy,_Nikita_Khrushchev_1961.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Sino%E2%80%93Soviet_split" class="mw-redirect" title="Sino–Soviet split">Sino–Soviet split</a> facilitated Russian and Chinese rapprochement with the U.S., and expanded East–West geopolitics into a tri-polar <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a> that allowed Premier <a href="/wiki/Nikita_Khrushchev" title="Nikita Khrushchev">Nikita Khrushchev</a> to meet with President <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy" title="John F. Kennedy">John F. Kennedy</a>, in June 1961.</div></div></div>
<p>Upon Allied victory concluding the Second World War (1939–1945), the members of the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Alliance_(World_War_II)" title="Grand Alliance (World War II)">Grand Alliance</a> resumed their expediently suppressed, pre-war <a href="/wiki/Geopolitics" title="Geopolitics">geopolitical rivalries</a> and ideological tensions, which disunity broke their <a href="/wiki/Anti-fascism" title="Anti-fascism">anti-fascist</a> wartime alliance into the anti–Communist <a href="/wiki/Western_Bloc" title="Western Bloc">Western Bloc</a> and the Communist <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Bloc" title="Eastern Bloc">Eastern Bloc</a>. The renewed competition for geopolitical <a href="/wiki/Hegemony" title="Hegemony">hegemony</a> resulted in the bi-polar <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a> (1945–1991), a protracted state of tension (military and diplomatic) between the US and the USSR, which often threatened a Russo–American <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_war" class="mw-redirect" title="Nuclear war">nuclear war</a>, but usually featured <a href="/wiki/Proxy_war" title="Proxy war">proxy wars</a> in the Third World.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The events that precipitated the Cold War in Europe were the Soviet and Yugoslav, Bulgarian and Albanian military interventions to the <a href="/wiki/Greek_Civil_War" title="Greek Civil War">Greek Civil War</a> (1944–1949), in behalf of the Greek Communists;<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Blockade" title="Berlin Blockade">Berlin Blockade</a> (1948–1949) by the Soviet Union. The event that precipitated the Cold War in continental Asia was the resumption of the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Civil_War" title="Chinese Civil War">Chinese Civil War</a> (1927–1949) fought between the anti-communist <a href="/wiki/Kuomintang" title="Kuomintang">Kuomintang</a> (KMT) and the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_China" title="Communist Party of China">Communist Party of China</a> (CPC); after military defeat exiled Generalissimo <a href="/wiki/Chiang_Kai-shek" title="Chiang Kai-shek">Chiang Kai-shek</a> and his KMT nationalist government to Formosa island (<a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a>), Mao Zedong established the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="People&#39;s Republic of China">People's Republic of China</a>, on 1 October 1949.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In Eastern Asia, the Cold War produced the <a href="/wiki/Korean_War" title="Korean War">Korean War</a> (1950–1953), the first proxy war between the Eastern Bloc and the Western Bloc, resulted from dual origins: (i) the nationalist Koreans' post-war resumption of their <a href="/wiki/Korean_Civil_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Korean Civil War">Korean Civil War</a>; and (ii) an imperial war for regional hegemony, sponsored by the US and the USSR.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> The international response to the North Korean invasion of South Korea was realised by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">United Nations Security Council</a> who voted for war — despite the absent Soviet Union — and authorised an international military expedition to intervene and expel the northern invaders from the south of Korea; and thus restore the geopolitical <i>status quo ante</i> of the Soviet and American <a href="/wiki/Division_of_Korea" title="Division of Korea">division of Korea</a> at the 38th Parallel of global latitude. Consequent to Chinese military intervention in behalf of Communist North Korea, the magnitude of the <a href="/wiki/Infantry" title="Infantry">infantry</a> warfare reached operational and geographic <a href="/wiki/Stalemate" title="Stalemate">stalemate</a> (July 1951 – July 1953); afterwards, the shooting war was ended with the <a href="/wiki/Korean_Armistice_Agreement" title="Korean Armistice Agreement">Korean Armistice Agreement</a> (27 July 1953); and the superpower Cold War in Asia then resumed as the <a href="/wiki/Korean_Demilitarized_Zone" title="Korean Demilitarized Zone">Korean Demilitarized Zone</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="De-Stalinization">De-Stalinization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marxism%E2%80%93Leninism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: De-Stalinization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Josip_Broz_Tito_uniform_portrait.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Josip_Broz_Tito_uniform_portrait.jpg/300px-Josip_Broz_Tito_uniform_portrait.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="451" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/13/Josip_Broz_Tito_uniform_portrait.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="319" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Josip_Broz_Tito_uniform_portrait.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>In 1948, <a href="/wiki/Josip_Broz_Tito" title="Josip Broz Tito">Tito</a>'s rejection of Soviet hegemony upon the <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Federal_Republic_of_Yugoslavia" title="Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia">Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia</a> provoked Stalin to expel the Yugoslav leader and Yugoslavia from the Eastern Bloc</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Yugoslavia">Yugoslavia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marxism%E2%80%93Leninism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Yugoslavia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the late 1940s, the geopolitics of the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_bloc" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern bloc">Eastern bloc</a> countries under the <a href="/wiki/Hegemony" title="Hegemony">hegemony</a> of Stalinist Russia featured an official-and-personal style of socialist diplomacy that failed Stalin and Tito, when Tito said "No." to subordinating Yugoslavia to Russia. In 1948, circumstance and cultural personality aggravated the matter into the <a href="/wiki/Yugoslav%E2%80%93Soviet_Split" class="mw-redirect" title="Yugoslav–Soviet Split">Yugoslav–Soviet Split</a> (1948–1955) that resulted from Tito's rejection of Stalin's demand to subordinate the <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Federal_Republic_of_Yugoslavia" title="Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia">Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia</a> to the geopolitical agenda (economic and military) of the USSR, i.e. Tito at Stalin's disposal.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Stalin punished Tito's refusal by denouncing the Yugoslav Communist leader as an <a href="/wiki/Revisionism_(Marxism)" title="Revisionism (Marxism)">ideological revisionist</a> of Marxism–Leninism; by denouncing Socialist Yugoslavia's practice of Titoism as <a href="/wiki/Deviationism" title="Deviationism">socialism deviated</a> from the cause of <a href="/wiki/World_communism" title="World communism">world communism</a>; and by expelling the Yugoslav communists from the <a href="/wiki/Cominform" title="Cominform">Communist Information Bureau</a> (Cominform). The break from Eastern-bloc Stalinism allowed the development of <a href="/wiki/Titoism" title="Titoism">Titoism</a>, socialism with Yugoslav characteristics, which allowed doing business with the capitalist West to develop the <a href="/wiki/Socialist_economy" class="mw-redirect" title="Socialist economy">socialist economy</a>, and the establishment of Socialist Yugoslavia's diplomatic and commercial relations with countries of the Eastern bloc and the Western bloc. Socialist Yugoslavia's international relations matured into the <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">Non-Aligned Movement</a> (1961) of countries without political allegiance to any <a href="/wiki/Power_bloc" class="mw-redirect" title="Power bloc">power bloc</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Soviet_Union">Soviet Union</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marxism%E2%80%93Leninism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Soviet Union">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>At the death of Stalin in 1953, <a href="/wiki/Nikita_Khrushchev" title="Nikita Khrushchev">Nikita Khrushchev</a> became leader of the Soviet Union and of the CPSU (Communist Party of the Soviet Union), and then consolidated an anti-Stalinist government. Three years later, in a secret meeting at the 20th congress of the CPSU, Khruschev denounced <a href="/wiki/Stalin" class="mw-redirect" title="Stalin">Stalin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stalinism" title="Stalinism">Stalinism</a> in the speech <i><a href="/wiki/On_the_Cult_of_Personality_and_Its_Consequences" title="On the Cult of Personality and Its Consequences">On the Cult of Personality and its Consequences</a></i> (25 February 1956) in which he specified and condemned Stalin's dictatorial excesses and abuses of power, such as the <a href="/wiki/Great_purge" class="mw-redirect" title="Great purge">Great purge</a> (1936–38) and the <a href="/wiki/Cult_of_personality" title="Cult of personality">cult of personality</a>. Khrushchev thus introduced the <a href="/wiki/De-Stalinisation" class="mw-redirect" title="De-Stalinisation">de-Stalinisation</a> of the Party and of the Soviet Union, which he realised with the dismantling of the <a href="/wiki/Gulag" title="Gulag">Gulag archipelago</a> of forced-labour camps and freeing the prisoners; allowing Soviet civil society greater political freedom of expression, especially for public intellectuals of the <a href="/wiki/Intelligentsia" title="Intelligentsia">Intelligentsia</a>, such as the novelist <a href="/wiki/Aleksandr_Solzhenitsyn" title="Aleksandr Solzhenitsyn">Aleksandr Solzhenitsyn</a>, whose literature obliquely criticised Stalin and the Stalinist <a href="/wiki/Police_state" title="Police state">police state</a>. De-Stalinization also ended Stalin's national-purpose policy of <a href="/wiki/Socialism_in_one_country" class="mw-redirect" title="Socialism in one country">socialism in one country</a>, which was replaced with <a href="/wiki/Proletarian_internationalism" title="Proletarian internationalism">proletarian internationalism</a>, by way of which Khrushchev re-committed the Soviet Union to <a href="/wiki/Permanent_revolution" title="Permanent revolution">permanent revolution</a> to realise <a href="/wiki/World_communism" title="World communism">world communism</a>. In that geopolitical vein, Khrushchev presented de-Stalinization as the restoration of <a href="/wiki/Leninism" title="Leninism">Leninism</a> as the official state ideology of the Soviet Union.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="China">China</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marxism%E2%80%93Leninism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: China">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the 1950s, the <a href="/wiki/De-Stalinisation" class="mw-redirect" title="De-Stalinisation">de-Stalinisation</a> of the Soviet Union was ideological bad news for the PRC, because Russian interpretations and applications of Leninism and Orthodox Marxism contradicted the Sinified Marxism–Leninism of Mao Zedong — his Chinese adaptations of Stalinist interpretation and praxis for establishing socialism in China. To realise that leap of Marxist faith in the development of Chinese socialism, the Communist Party of China developed Maoism (the <a href="/wiki/Maoism" title="Maoism">Thought of Mao Zedong</a>) as the official state ideology of the People's Republic of China. As the specifically Chinese development of Marxism–Leninism, Maoism illuminated the cultural differences between the European-Russian and the Asian-Chinese interpretations and practical applications of <a href="/wiki/Leninism" title="Leninism">Leninism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Orthodox_Marxism" title="Orthodox Marxism">Orthodox Marxism</a> in each country. The political differences then provoked geopolitical, ideological, and nationalist tensions, which derived from the different stages of development, between the urban society of the industrialised USSR and the agricultural society of the pre-industrial PRC. The theory-vs-praxis arguments escalated to theoretic disputes about <a href="/wiki/Revisionism_(Marxism)" title="Revisionism (Marxism)">Marxist revisionism</a>, and provoked the <a href="/wiki/Sino-Soviet_split" title="Sino-Soviet split">Sino-Soviet split</a> (1956–1966), and the PRC and the USSR broke their international relations (diplomatic and political, cultural and economic).<sup id="cite_ref-World_History_2000._p._769_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_History_2000._p._769-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Consequent to the Sino-Soviet split, the pragmatic PRC established politics of <i><a href="/wiki/D%C3%A9tente" title="Détente">détente</a></i> with the US, in effort to publicly challenge the USSR for leadership of the international communist movement. Mao's pragmatism permitted geopolitical rapprochement and facilitated US President <a href="/wiki/Richard_Nixon%27s_1972_visit_to_China" title="Richard Nixon&#39;s 1972 visit to China">Richard Nixon's 1972 visit to China</a>, which subsequently ended the US policy of the existence to "two Chinas", when the United States sponsored the People's Republic of China to replace the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of China">Republic of China</a> (Taiwan) as the representative of the Chinese people at the United Nations; in the due course of Sino-American rapprochement, the PRC also assumed membership in the <a href="/wiki/Security_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="Security Council">Security Council</a> of the UN.<sup id="cite_ref-World_History_2000._p._769_20-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_History_2000._p._769-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> In the post–Mao period of Sino-American <i>détente</i>, the <a href="/wiki/Deng_Xiaoping" title="Deng Xiaoping">Deng Xiaoping</a> government (1982–1987) effected policies of <a href="/wiki/Economic_liberalism" title="Economic liberalism">economic liberalisation</a> that allowed continual growth for the Chinese economy. The ideological justification is <a href="/wiki/Socialism_with_Chinese_characteristics" title="Socialism with Chinese characteristics">socialism with Chinese characteristics</a>, the Chinese adaption of Marxism–Leninism.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span id="Marxist.E2.80.93Leninist_revolution"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Marxist–Leninist_revolution">Marxist–Leninist revolution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marxism%E2%80%93Leninism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Marxist–Leninist revolution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CheyFidel.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/CheyFidel.jpg/300px-CheyFidel.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="401" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/CheyFidel.jpg/450px-CheyFidel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/CheyFidel.jpg/600px-CheyFidel.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1197" data-file-height="1600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CheyFidel.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Che_Guevara" title="Che Guevara">Che Guevara</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fidel_Castro" title="Fidel Castro">Fidel Castro</a>, leader of the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Cuba" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of Cuba">Republic of Cuba</a> from 1959 to 2008, successfully led to victory the <a href="/wiki/Cuban_Revolution" title="Cuban Revolution">Cuban Revolution</a> in 1959</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Latin_America">Latin America</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marxism%E2%80%93Leninism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Latin America">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<dl><dt>Cuba</dt></dl>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Cuban_Revolution" title="Cuban Revolution">Cuban Revolution</a> (1956–59), led by <a href="/wiki/Fidel_Castro" title="Fidel Castro">Fidel Castro</a> and <a href="/wiki/Che_Guevara" title="Che Guevara">Ché Guevara</a>, deposed the régime (1952–1959) of <a href="/wiki/Fulgencio_Batista" title="Fulgencio Batista">Fulgencio Batista</a>, and established the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Cuba" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of Cuba">Republic of Cuba</a>, a socialist state formally recognised by the Soviet Union.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> In response, the United States launched a <i>coup d'état</i> against the Castro government; in 1961, the CIA's unsuccessful <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Pigs_invasion" class="mw-redirect" title="Bay of Pigs invasion">Bay of Pigs invasion</a> (17 April 1961), by anti-communist Cuban exiles, which attack impelled the Republic of Cuba to side with the USSR; and, in 1962, there occurred the <a href="/wiki/Cuban_missile_crisis" class="mw-redirect" title="Cuban missile crisis">Cuban missile crisis</a> (22–28 October 1962), about US opposition to Socialist Cuba being armed with Soviet nuclear missiles. The US and the USSR jointly resolved the nuclear-missile crisis by respectively removing American nuclear-armed missiles from Turkey and Italy, and Soviet missiles from Cuba.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dt>Nicaragua</dt></dl>
<p>In 1979, the <a href="/wiki/Sandinista_National_Liberation_Front" title="Sandinista National Liberation Front">Sandinista National Liberation Front</a> (FSLN), led by <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Ortega" title="Daniel Ortega">Daniel Ortega</a>, won the <a href="/wiki/Nicaraguan_Revolution" title="Nicaraguan Revolution">Nicaraguan Revolution</a> (1961–1990) against the government of <a href="/wiki/Anastasio_Somoza_Debayle" title="Anastasio Somoza Debayle">Anastasio Somoza Debayle</a> (1 December 1974 – 17 July 1979); within months, the new government of U.S. Pres. Ronald Reagan sponsored the counter-revolutionary <a href="/wiki/Contras" title="Contras">Contras</a> in the secret <a href="/wiki/Contra_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Contra War">Contra War</a> (1979–1990) against socialist Nicaragua. In 1989, the Contra War concluded with the signing of the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Tela_Accord&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Tela Accord (page does not exist)">Tela Accord</a>, and the subsequent demobilization of the Contra armies and the FSLN army.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> In 1990, a second national election installed to government a majority of anti–Sandinista political parties, to whom the FSLN handed political power.
</p>
<dl><dt>Grenada</dt></dl>
<p>In 1983, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_invasion_of_Grenada" title="United States invasion of Grenada">US Invasion of Grenada</a> (25–29 October 1983 ) thwarted the assumption of power by the elected government of the <a href="/wiki/New_Jewel_Movement" title="New Jewel Movement">New Jewel Movement</a> (1973–1983), a Marxist–Leninist vanguard party led by <a href="/wiki/Maurice_Bishop" title="Maurice Bishop">Maurice Bishop</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Salvadoran_Civil_War" title="Salvadoran Civil War">Salvadoran Civil War</a> (1979–1992) featured the popularly supported <a href="/wiki/Farabundo_Mart%C3%AD_National_Liberation_Front" title="Farabundo Martí National Liberation Front">Farabundo Martí National Liberation Front</a>, an organisation of left-wing parties fighting against the right-wing military government of El Salvador.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="North_America">North America</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marxism%E2%80%93Leninism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: North America">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<dl><dt>Canada</dt></dl>
<p>In 1970, the <a href="/wiki/October_Crisis" title="October Crisis">October Crisis</a> (5 October – 28 December 1970) occurred in Canada, a brief revolution in the province of <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">Québec</a>, where the actions of the separatist <i><a href="/wiki/Front_de_lib%C3%A9ration_du_Qu%C3%A9bec" title="Front de libération du Québec">Front de libération du Québec</a></i> (FLQ; Front for the Liberation of Québec) featured the kidnap of James Cross, the British Trade Commissioner in Canada, and the killing of <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Laporte" title="Pierre Laporte">Pierre Laporte</a>, the Quebec government minister. The political manifesto of the FLQ condemned English-Canadian imperialism in French Québec, and called for a separate <i>Québecois</i> socialist state. The Canadian government's harsh response included the suspension of civil liberties in Quebec, which compelled the FLQ leaders' flight to Socialist Cuba.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Eastern_Asia">Eastern Asia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marxism%E2%80%93Leninism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Eastern Asia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nlfmainforce.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Nlfmainforce.jpg/300px-Nlfmainforce.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="225" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Nlfmainforce.jpg/450px-Nlfmainforce.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/3f/Nlfmainforce.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="375" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nlfmainforce.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The National Liberation Front (NLF): <a href="/wiki/Viet_Cong" title="Viet Cong">Viet Cong</a> guerillas during the Vietnam War</div></div></div>
<dl><dt>Vietnam</dt></dl>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">Vietnam War</a> (1945–1975) was the second East–West war that occurred in Asia during the Cold War. After the <a href="/wiki/Vi%E1%BB%87t_Minh" title="Việt Minh">Việt Minh</a>, led by <a href="/wiki/Ho_Chi_Minh" title="Ho Chi Minh">Ho Chi Minh</a>, defeated the French re-establishment of European colonialism in Viet Nam, the United States replaced France as the Western power supporting the client-state <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Vietnam" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of Vietnam">Republic of Vietnam</a> (1955–1975). Despite military superiority, the U.S. failed to safeguard South Vietnam from the <a href="/wiki/Viet_Cong" title="Viet Cong">Viet Cong</a>, the guerrilla army sponsored by North Vietnam. In 1968, North Vietnam launched the <a href="/wiki/Tet_Offensive" title="Tet Offensive">Tet Offensive</a>, which, although a military failure, was successful <a href="/wiki/Psychological_warfare" title="Psychological warfare">psychological warfare</a> that decisively turned international public opinion against the U.S's intervention to the Vietnamese civil war, which led to military withdrawal from Vietnam in 1973, and the subsequent <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_Saigon" title="Fall of Saigon">Fall of Saigon</a> to the North Vietnamese army, on 1 May 1975.
</p>
<dl><dt>Cambodia</dt></dl>
<p>Consequent to the <a href="/wiki/Cambodian_Civil_War" title="Cambodian Civil War">Cambodian Civil War</a> and in coalition with Prince <a href="/wiki/Norodom_Sihanouk" title="Norodom Sihanouk">Norodom Sihanouk</a>, the native Cambodian Communists, the Maoist <a href="/wiki/Khmer_Rouge" title="Khmer Rouge">Khmer Rouge</a> (1951–1999) led by <a href="/wiki/Pol_Pot" title="Pol Pot">Pol Pot</a>, established <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Kampuchea" title="Democratic Kampuchea">Democratic Kampuchea</a> (1975–1982), a Marxist–Leninist state that featured <a href="/wiki/Class_conflict" title="Class conflict">class warfare</a> to restructure the society of old Cambodia; to be effected and realised with the abolishment of <a href="/wiki/Money" title="Money">money</a> and private property, the outlawing of religion, the killing of the <a href="/wiki/Intelligentsia" title="Intelligentsia">intelligentsia</a> and compulsory manual labour for the <a href="/wiki/Middle_class" title="Middle class">middle classes</a> by way of death-squad <a href="/wiki/State_terrorism" title="State terrorism">state terrorism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>To eliminate Western cultural influence, Kampuchea expelled all foreigners and effected the destruction of the urban <a href="/wiki/Bourgeoisie" title="Bourgeoisie">bourgeoisie</a> of old Cambodia, first by displacing the population of the capital city, Phnom Penh; and then by displacing the national populace to work farmlands to increase food supplies. Meanwhile, the Khmer Rouge purged Kampuchea of internal enemies (social class and political, cultural and ethnic) at <a href="/wiki/Khmer_Rouge_Killing_Fields" title="Khmer Rouge Killing Fields">the killing fields</a>, the scope of which became <a href="/wiki/Crimes_against_humanity" title="Crimes against humanity">crimes against humanity</a>, which killed 2,700,000 people by mass murder and genocide.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-dict_192193_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dict_192193-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> That social restructuring of Cambodia included attacks against the Vietnamese ethnic minority in Kampuchea, which aggravated the historical, ethnic rivalries between the Viet and the Khmer peoples. Beginning in September 1977, Kampuchea and the <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Republic_of_Vietnam" class="mw-redirect" title="Socialist Republic of Vietnam">Socialist Republic of Vietnam</a> continually engaged in border clashes. In 1978, Vietnam invaded Kampuchea and captured Phnom Penh in January 1979, deposed the Maoist Khmer Rouge from government and established the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambodian_Liberation_Front_for_National_Renewal&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Cambodian Liberation Front for National Renewal (page does not exist)">Cambodian Liberation Front for National Renewal</a> as the government of Cambodia.<sup id="cite_ref-dict_192193_98-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dict_192193-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Africa">Africa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marxism%E2%80%93Leninism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Africa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In Africa, during the 1968–1980 period, Angola, Benin, and the Republic of Congo, Ethiopia, Mozambique, Somalia and Zimbabwe became Marxist–Leninist states governed by their respective native peoples; Marxist–Leninist guerrillas fought the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Colonial_War" title="Portuguese Colonial War">Portuguese Colonial War</a> in three countries, <a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">Angola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guinea-Bissau" title="Guinea-Bissau">Guinea-Bissau</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mozambique" title="Mozambique">Mozambique</a>; overthrew of the monarchy of <a href="/wiki/Haile_Selassie" title="Haile Selassie">Haile Selassie</a> and established the <a href="/wiki/Derg" title="Derg">Derg</a> government (1974–1987) of the Coordinating Committee of the Armed Forces, Police and Territorial Army in Ethiopia; <a href="/wiki/Robert_Mugabe" title="Robert Mugabe">Robert Mugabe</a> led the successful civil war to overthrow white-minority rule in <a href="/wiki/Rhodesia" title="Rhodesia">Rhodesia</a> (1965–1979) and established <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe" title="Zimbabwe">Zimbabwe</a>. In South Africa, the anti-communist, white-minority government—based upon the official racist policy of <a href="/wiki/Apartheid" title="Apartheid">apartheid</a> — caused much geopolitical tension between the US and the USSR. In 1976, anti-communism became morally untenable for the West when the South African government killed 176 people (students and adults) in suppressing the <a href="/wiki/Soweto_uprising" title="Soweto uprising">Soweto uprising</a> (June 1976), which protested Afrikaner <a href="/wiki/Cultural_imperialism" title="Cultural imperialism">cultural imperialism</a>, the imposition of <a href="/wiki/Afrikaans" title="Afrikaans">Afrikaans</a> (a European Germanic language) as the language for teaching school and as the language that black South Africans must speak to white people; and the police assassination of <a href="/wiki/Steven_Biko" class="mw-redirect" title="Steven Biko">Steven Biko</a> (September 1977), a leader of the <a href="/wiki/Internal_resistance_to_apartheid" title="Internal resistance to apartheid">internal resistance to apartheid</a> in South Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marxism%E2%80%93Leninism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
